The Forelock Metaphor: Rhetoric and Theology in Usul
Explains metaphor for objectives' dependence on Allah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the rhetorical device of isti'ara bilkinnaya in a usul text and explain how it conveys the theological point of divine control over all objectives.

Core Idea
The forelock metaphor shows that all objectives are under Allah's control.

This lesson unpacks a beautifully crafted line from the matn: 'wa nawasi al-maqasidi mufawwadatun ilayk' (And the forelocks of the objectives are entrusted to You). By analyzing the author's use of metonymical metaphor, we see how usul texts employ sophisticated Arabic rhetoric to embed theological meaning. Understanding this deepens our appreciation of how the Hanafi school communicates legal principles through layered language.

Guided Path
1
Define the key terms
Identify the meanings of 'nawasi' (forelocks), 'maqasid' (objectives), and 'mufawwada' (entrusted/referred back) as given in the passage.
These terms are building blocks for the metaphor.
2
Recognize the two metaphors
The author draws two comparisons: (1) principles (mabadi) are like mounts controlled by reins, and (2) objectives (maqasid) are like wild animals controlled by forelocks. Identify the compared and the compared-to.
Only the rein/forelock is mentioned, not the mount/animal.
3
Identify the rhetorical device
The commentator labels this 'isti'ara bilkinnaya' (metonymical metaphor) and 'takhayyuliya' (imaginative metaphor). Explain why only a part of the compared-to is mentioned.
This device emphasizes the essential point of control.
4
Understand the theological import
The metaphor underscores that achieving any objective depends entirely on Allah's will. The forelock is seized to control the animal; similarly, Allah holds the forelock of every purpose.
This reinforces tawakkul and divine omnipotence in usul reasoning.
5
Connect to the broader usul context
Reflect on why such rhetorical flourish appears in a usul text. The author is not merely decorating; he is shaping the reader's mindset before engaging with legal derivation.
Maqasid al-shari'a is a key concept; the metaphor asserts that these purposes are ultimately subject to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ونواصى المقاصد مفوضة الیک : ۔ اس کا قول نواصی، ناصیہ کی جمع ہے موئے پیشانی کو کہتے ہیں یا ہر چہار طرف بال اگنے کی منتہاء کو کہتے ہیں۔ مقاصد ، مقصد کی جمع ہے مطلب کے معنی میں ہے۔ مفوضته ، تفویض کا اسم مفعول مؤنث ، ردالیہ یا مردودۃ کے معنی میں ہے۔ ان دونوں جملوں میں حضرت مصنف نے جن براعت ظاہرہ اور فصاحت و بلاغت کا جو ہر دکھلایا ہے تفطن پرمخفی نہیں ۔ یادر ہے کہ مصنف نے مبادی ( اسباب) کو ان مراکب سے تشبیہ دی ہے جو سواروں کو منزل مقصود تک لے جاتے ہیں مگر مراکب جو مشبہ یہ ہے کا ذکر نہیں کیا ہے صرف مشبہ جو مبادی ہے کا ذکر کیا ہے البتہ مشبہ بہ کے لوازم میں سے عنان کو ذکر کیا ہے فن میں اس طرز تحریر کو استعارہ بالکنایہ کہتے ہیں پھر مبادی کے لئے اعنہ کا اثبات استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے، اسی طرح اہم ترین مقصد مشکل فن اور لابنخل مسائل کو شریر اور بدکنے والے جانوروں سے تشبیہ دی جو بمشکل ہاتھ آتے ہیں جن کو ان کے پیشانی کے بال پکڑ کر قابو میں کیا جاتا ہے مگر مشبہ بہ کو ذکر نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ اس کے لوازم میں سے نواصی کو ذکر کیا ہے یہ بھی استعارہ بالکنایہ ہے اور پھر مقاصد کے لئے نواصی کا اثبات استعارہ تخیلیہ ہے۔
His saying: 'And the forelocks of the objectives are entrusted to You.' He says: 'Nawasi' is the plural of 'nasiya,' meaning the hair of the forehead, or the end from which hair grows on all four sides. 'Maqasid' is the plural of 'maqsid,' meaning intention/objective. 'Mufawwadatun' is the feminine passive participle of 'tafwid,' meaning 'referred back' or 'returned.' There is no doubt that in these two sentences, the author (al-Musannif) has demonstrated remarkable eloquence and brilliance. Note: The author likened the principles (causes) to mounts that carry riders to the destination, but he did not mention the thing compared (the mount); he only mentioned the thing compared to (the principles), but he mentioned one of the necessary parts of the compared-to thing, namely the rein. In rhetoric, this style is called 'isti'ara bilkinnaya' (metonymical metaphor). Then, the affirmation of reins for principles is a 'takhayyuliya' (imaginative) metaphor. Similarly, he likened the most important objective – the difficult art and intricate issues – to wild, restless animals that are difficult to catch, which are controlled by seizing the forelock hair. But he did not mention the compared-to thing; rather, he mentioned one of its necessary parts, the forelock. This is also 'isti'ara bilkinnaya,' and then the affirmation of forelocks for objectives is a 'takhayyuliya' metaphor.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage analyzes the second part of the matn: 'wa nawasi al-maqasidi mufawwadatun ilayk' (And the forelocks of the objectives are entrusted to You). The commentator defines 'nawasi' (forelocks), 'maqasid' (objectives), and 'mufawwada' (entrusted). He then highlights the literary device used by the author (Musannif): the principles (mabadi) are compared to mounts that carry riders to their goal, but only the rein (a part of the mount) is mentioned; this is a metonymical metaphor (isti'ara bilkinnaya). Similarly, difficult objectives and complicated issues are compared to wild animals that are controlled by their forelocks, and only the forelock is mentioned. This emphasizes that just as the forelock of an animal is seized to control it, the achievement of any objective is entirely in Allah's control. The passage demonstrates the rhetorical sophistication of the matn.

Key Terms
نواصی (nawasi): Forelocks; plural of 'nasiya' (forehead hair). Used metaphorically to indicate control.
مقاصد (maqasid): Objectives; plural of 'maqsid' (intention, aim). In usul, often refers to the purposes of the Law (maqasid al-shari'a).
استعارہ بالکنایہ (isti'ara bilkinnaya): Metonymical metaphor; a figure of speech where only a necessary part of the compared-to thing is mentioned.
مفوضة (mufawwadatun): Feminine passive participle of tafwid; meaning 'entrusted' or 'referred back'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What rhetorical device is used when the author mentions only the rein (not the mount) to imply control over principles?
A) Isti'ara tammah (complete metaphor)
B) Isti'ara bilkinnaya (metonymical metaphor)
C) Haqiqah (literal expression)
D) Majaz mursal (synecdoche)

Key Takeaway
The forelock metaphor in usul texts is a rhetorical device that asserts divine sovereignty over all legal objectives, reminding the scholar that even the most intricate derivations are subject to Allah's will.

Resolving the Apparent Inconsistency in Ibn al-Humam's Statements on Qiyas
Resolving apparent inconsistency in Ibn al-Humam's statements about qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to resolve the apparent contradiction in Ibn al-Humam's statements by distinguishing between two definitions of qiyas and explaining the discipline of hujjiyya under each.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Humam's statements are consistent when qiyas is defined as either an act of ijtihad or divine equality.

The great Hanafi scholar Ibn al-Humam was accused of contradicting himself on the hujjiyya of qiyas—claiming it is a fiqh issue in one place and no discipline in another. This lesson clarifies that his statements refer to two different definitions of qiyas. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping how Hanafi usul classifies the foundations of qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
Note that Ibn al-Humam is reported to have said hujjiyya of qiyas is a fiqh issue and also that it belongs to no discipline. This seems inconsistent.
The contradiction is the starting point; it must be resolved by examining the context.
2
Recognize the two definitions of qiyas
The passage clarifies two definitions: qiyas as 'the act of the mujtahid' (exerting inference) and qiyas as 'divine equality' between original and branch in the cause.
These definitions lead to different classifications of hujjiyya.
3
Analyze each definition's implication for hujjiyya
Under the first definition, hujjiyya is a theoretical issue requiring ijtihad, hence it belongs to fiqh. Under the second definition, divine equality is a religious necessity (daruriyya diniyya), not a theoretical discipline, so it belongs to no discipline.
This key step resolves the contradiction.
4
Conclude the consistency
Both statements are true depending on which definition is intended. The attribution of inconsistency is incorrect.
Final conclusion: Ibn al-Humam's statements are consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مصنف نے اپنے قول " ومن قال پر حاشیہ نگاری کرتے ہوئے کہا ہے ۔ اى القائل ابن الهمام " انتهى
تحقیقی جواب: تحقیق یہ ہے کہ شیخ ابن الہام کی طرف یہ انتساب اور ان کے کلام میں اضطراب نہیں ہے چنانچہ انہوں نے اپنی کتاب تحریر کے مقدمہ میں اپنے قول انها من الفقہ" کے بعد کہا ہے وهو في القياس على تقدير كونه فعل المجتهد واما على انه المساواة الكـائـنـة عـن تـسـويـة الـلـه تـعـالـى بـيـن الاصـل و الـفـرع في العلة فليست مسئلة لانها ضرورية دينية یعنی ہم نے جو یہ کہا ہے کہ حجیت قیاس کا مسئلہ فقہیہ ہے اصولیہ نہیں ہے وہ اس نقد پر ہے کہ قیاس کو فعل مجہتد قرار دیا جائے اور تعریف میں یہ کہا جائے کہ استنباط حکم کے لئے قوت استنباط کو صرف کرنا قیاس ہے لیکن اگر قیاس کی یہ تعریف کی جائے کہ قیاس اس مساوات کا نام ہے جو اصل و فرع کے درمیان منجانب اللہ علت میں مساوات پیدا ہونے سے ہوا تو اس تعریف کے مطابق حجیت قیاس کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہیں رہ جائے گا اس لئے کہ مساوات مذکورہ حجیت ضروریات دینیہ میں سے ہے۔ حاصل کلام یہ کہ شیخ ابن ہمام نے جہاں یہ کہا کہ حجیت قیاس فقہ کا مسئلہ ہے تو اس لئے کہ قیاس فعل مجتہد ہے اور جہاں یہ کہا یہ کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہیں ہے تو اس لئے کہ قیاس مساوات الہیہ سے عبارت ہے اور مساوات الہیہ کے ضروریات دینیہ ہونے میں شک نہیں اس لئے کہ اس تقدیر پر حجیت قیاس کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کسی فن کا مسئلہ ہونے کے لئے اس کا نظری ہونا ضروری ہے۔ غرض یہ نقل و انتساب بیجا و غیر صحیح ہے۔
The author, while annotating his statement 'And whoever said', said: 'i.e., the one who said is Ibn al-Humam'. End. The investigative answer: The investigation is that this attribution to Shaykh Ibn al-Humam and inconsistency in his speech is not present. Indeed, he said in the introduction of his book Al-Tahrir after his statement 'it is from fiqh': 'And it is regarding qiyas on the estimation that it is the act of the mujtahid. But if it is the equality arising from Allah's equalization between the original and the branch in the cause, then it is not an issue because it is a religious necessity.' Meaning: What we said that the issue of hujjiyya of qiyas is fiqhi and not usuli is on the condition that qiyas is considered the act of the mujtahid, and it is defined as 'expending the power of inference to deduce a ruling is qiyas'. But if qiyas is defined as 'the name for that equality which occurs between the original and the branch due to the equality from Allah regarding the cause', then according to this definition, the hujjiyya of qiyas will no longer be an issue of any discipline, because the mentioned equality is of the religious necessities. The upshot is that where Ibn al-Humam said that hujjiyya of qiyas is an issue of fiqh, it is because qiyas is the act of the mujtahid; and where he said it is not an issue of any discipline, it is because qiyas is the divine equality, and there is no doubt that divine equality is of the religious necessities. Therefore, on this estimation, hujjiyya of qiyas will not be an issue of any discipline, because for something to be an issue of a discipline, it must be theoretical. In short, this transmission and attribution is out of place and incorrect.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage resolves an apparent contradiction in the statements of Shaykh Ibn al-Humam, a prominent Hanafi scholar. The objection was that he claimed in one place that hujjiyya of qiyas belongs to fiqh, and in another that it belongs to no discipline. The author clarifies that Ibn al-Humam's statements are consistent when considering two definitions of qiyas. If qiyas is defined as the act of the mujtahid (a human action), then its hujjiyya is a fiqh issue. But if qiyas is defined as the divinely ordained equality between original and branch in terms of the cause ('illa), then that equality is a religious necessity (daruriyya diniyya) and thus not a theoretical issue of any discipline. The attribution of inconsistency is therefore incorrect.

Key Terms
فعل المجتهد (fi'l al-mujtahid): Qiyas considered as the act of ijtihad performed by the mujtahid.
مساواة إلهية (musawat ilahiyya): The divine equality between original and branch in terms of the cause, established by Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, under which definition of qiyas is its hujjiyya considered a fiqhi issue?
A) When qiyas is defined as divine equality
B) When qiyas is defined as the act of the mujtahid
C) When qiyas is defined as a religious necessity
D) Under both definitions

Key Takeaway
The apparent inconsistency in Ibn al-Humam's statements resolves once we distinguish between qiyas as a human act (fiqh issue) and as divine equality (religious necessity).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Authority of Ijma' and Qiyas: A Theological or Legal Question?
Classification of hujjiyya of ijma' and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi position on whether the authority of ijma' and qiyas belongs to 'ilm al-kalam or usul al-fiqh, and explain the reason for the usuli's engagement with these sources.

Core Idea
The authority of ijma' and qiyas is theological, but usulis discuss it because it is disputed.

In this passage, the commentator addresses a fundamental question: is the authority (hujjiyya) of ijma' (consensus) and qiyas (analogy) part of usul al-fiqh or 'ilm al-kalam? The text presents a dispute among scholars, including Ibn al-Humam, and then resolves it by clarifying that while the authority itself is a matter of belief (kalam), usulis must discuss it due to severe disagreement in the Ummah. This lesson will guide you through the arguments and the counterobjection, and help you understand the distinction between theological foundations and legal methodology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central dispute
Read the first part of the passage to understand the two conflicting views: some (including a reported view of Ibn al-Humam) say that the authority of qiyas is a fiqh issue because qiyas is an act of the mujtahid; others say it is not a matter of any discipline because it rests on divine equality, which is a necessary matter of religion. The author rejects both extremes.
The author uses the phrase 'bal al-haqq anna min al-kalam' to affirm the correct view.
2
Grasp the author's ruling: it belongs to kalam
The text then states that the truth is that the authority of ijma' and qiyas is from 'ilm al-kalam, just like the authority of the Quran and Sunnah. The reason: what is sought from it is belief (i'tiqad), not a practical ruling. Usulis only engage with it as a principium (mabda').
Note the parallel drawn with the Quran and Sunnah: their authority is universally accepted as kalam, yet usulis do not discuss it because there is no disagreement.
3
Recognise the objection
An imagined objector argues: if all proofs belong to kalam, why do usulis only discuss the authority of ijma' and qiyas but not of the Quran and Sunnah? They should be consistent.
This objection highlights the apparent inconsistency.
4
Understand the answer: disagreement is the key
The author answers that the Quran and Sunnah are unanimously accepted by the entire Ummah, so there is no need to prove their authority. In contrast, ijma' and qiyas are heavily disputed by various sects (Mu'tazila, Zahiris, Khawarij, etc.). Therefore, usulis must establish their authority to build the discipline of usul al-fiqh upon them.
This explanation shows that the usuli's engagement is driven by necessity, not by a change in the nature of the subject.
5
Apply the distinction
Now, consider any new source or legal principle. Ask: Does its authority require belief (i'tiqad)? If yes, it belongs to kalam. But if there is disagreement about its validity, usulis may need to discuss it as a prerequisite for usul al-fiqh.
This step cements the conceptual boundary between theological foundation and legal theory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کرنا قیاس ہے لیکن اگر قیاس کی یہ تعریف کی جائے کہ قیاس اس مساوات کا نام ہے جو اصل و فرع کے درمیان منجانب اللہ علت میں مساوات پیدا ہونے سے ہوا تو اس تعریف کے مطابق حجیت قیاس کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہیں رہ جائے گا اس لئے کہ مساوات مذکورہ حجیت ضروریات دینیہ میں سے ہے۔ حاصل کلام یہ کہ شیخ ابن ہمام نے جہاں یہ کہا کہ حجیت قیاس فقہ کا مسئلہ ہے تو اس لئے کہ قیاس فعل مجتہد ہے اور جہاں یہ کہا یہ کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہیں ہے تو اس لئے کہ قیاس مساوات الہیہ سے عبارت ہے اور مساوات الہیہ کے ضروریات دینیہ ہونے میں شک نہیں اس لئے کہ اس تقدیر پر حجیت قیاس کسی فن کا مسئلہ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ کسی فن کا مسئلہ ہونے کے لئے اس کا نظری ہونا ضروری ہے۔ غرض یہ نقل و انتساب بیجا و غیر صحیح ہے۔

قوله بل الحق انه من الكلام كحجية الكتاب والسنة. حجیت اجماع وقیاس کے بارے میں اختلاف علماء ذکر کرنے کے بعد مندرجہ بالا عبارت میں اب اپنا فیصلہ ومحاکمہ پیش کرتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں کہ حق یہ ہے کہ حجیت اجماع و قیاس علم کلام کا مسئلہ ہے جس میں مبدا و معاد کے احوال سے بحث ہوتی ہے جس طرح ادلہ اربعہ میں سے حجیت کتاب وسنت کا مسئلہ بالا تفاق علم کلام ہی کا مسئلہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس سے مطلوب صرف اعتقاد رہا ہے اصولیین کا اس سے اشتغال رکھنا تو وہ بروجہ مبدئیت ہے چنانچہ محمد بن امیر الحاج نے تقریر میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ ابن ہمام حجیت قیاس کے مسئلہ کو مسائل کلامیہ میں مانتے ہیں اسی طرف صاحب تلویح کا بھی رجحان معلوم ہوتا ہے چونکہ انہوں نے کہا ہے کہ احکام شرعیہ نظریہ کو اعتقادیہ اور اصلیہ کہتے ہیں جیسے اجماع کا حجت ہونا مثلاً اس لئے حجیت اجماع و قیاس بھی علم کلام سے ہے۔

قوله - ولكن تعرض الاصولى لحجيتهما فقط اعتراض : ۔ مصنف کے محاکمہ مذکورہ پر اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے کہ جب کل ادلہ کی حجیت علم کلام ہی سے ہے فقہ واصول فقہ سے کوئی نہیں تو ظاہر ہے کہ اصولیین کو اس سے کوئی غرض نہیں ہونا چاہئے نہ اصول فقہ میں حجیت قیاس کے مسئلہ کو چھیڑنا چاہئے جس طرح یہ حضرات حجیت کتاب وسنت کے مسئلہ کو نہیں چھیڑتے، البتہ اگر حجیت اجماع وقیاس کے مسئلہ کو یہ حضرات بطور مبدئیت واصالت ذکر کرتے ہیں تو اسی طرح حجیت کتاب و سنت کے مسئلہ کو بھی بطور مبدئیت واصالت ذکر کرنا چاہئے ۔ آخر کار صرف حجیت اجماع وقیاس کے مسئلہ کو ذکر کرنے کی کیا وجہ ہے؟

جواب: ۔ مصنف نے اپنے قول مذکور ولکن تعرض الاصولی سے دیا ہے۔ اس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ قرآن وسنت کی حجیت تمام امت محمدیہ کے نزدیک مسلم و متفق علیہ ہے اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں اس لئے اصولیین اس کو نہیں چھیڑتے ، اس کے برعکس حجیت اجماع و قیاس میں بین الامتہ شدید اختلاف پایا جاتا ہے چنانچہ نظام معتزلی اور بعض روافض و خوارج نے سرے سے اجماع ہی سے انکار کر دیا۔ داؤد ظاہری اور ان کے متبعین نے اور ایک روایت کے مطابق امام احمد نے اجماع کو صحابہ کے ساتھ مختص کردیا ہے، شیعہ میں زیدیہ اور امامیہ نے صرف عزت رسول کے اجماع کو معتبر مانا ہے اسی طرح اہل الظواہر نے حجیت قیاس سے انکار کیا ہے اسی وجہ سے، حجیت اجماع و قیاس کے اثبات کو اصولیین نے ضروری سمجھا چونکہ اجماع وقیاس کی حجیت میں اس قدر شدید اختلاف و نزاع مسائل اصولیہ میں اختلاف و نزاع کا باعث موجب ہوا کیونکہ مسائل اصولیہ کی بنیاد حجیت اجماع وقیاس کی دیوار پر قائم ہے اس لئے خاص طور پر ان دونوں کے ذکر کی ضرورت پڑی اور کتاب وسنت میں چونکہ کوئی اختلاف نہیں اس لئے اس کے ذکر کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں۔
To perform qiyas is qiyas, but if qiyas is defined as the name for the equality that occurs between the original and the branch due to an equality in the cause from Allah, then according to this definition, the authority (hujjiyya) of qiyas will not remain a matter of any discipline, because the mentioned equality is among the necessary matters of religion. The summary is that Shaykh Ibn al-Humam, when he said that the authority of qiyas is a matter of fiqh, it is because qiyas is the act of a mujtahid, and when he said that it is not a matter of any discipline, it is because qiyas consists of divine equality, and there is no doubt that divine equality is among the necessary matters of religion, because on this assumption the authority of qiyas would not be a matter of any discipline, since for something to be a matter of a discipline, it must be theoretical. In short, this attribution is misplaced and incorrect.

His statement: 'Rather the truth is that it is from kalam, like the authority of the Book and the Sunnah.' After mentioning the disagreement of scholars regarding the authority of ijma' and qiyas, in the above statement he now presents his judgment and ruling, saying that the truth is that the authority of ijma' and qiyas is a matter of 'ilm al-kalam, in which the conditions of the beginning and the end are discussed, just as among the four proofs, the authority of the Book and Sunnah is, by agreement, a matter of 'ilm al-kalam, because only belief is sought from it. The engagement of the usulis with it is by way of principality. As Muhammad ibn Amir al-Hajj mentioned in al-Taqrir that Ibn al-Humam considers the issue of the authority of qiyas among the kalam issues. The author of al-Talwih also seems to incline to this, since he said that theoretical Shari'a rulings are called doctrinal and fundamental, such as the authority of ijma' for example, so the authority of ijma' and qiyas is also from 'ilm al-kalam.

His statement: 'But the usuli only discusses their authority' is an objection. An objection is raised against the author's ruling mentioned: when the authority of all proofs is from 'ilm al-kalam and not from fiqh or usul al-fiqh, then obviously usulis should have no interest in it, nor should they raise the issue of the authority of qiyas in usul al-fiqh, just as these scholars do not discuss the authority of the Book and Sunnah. However, if they mention the issue of the authority of ijma' and qiyas as a principality and origin, then they should also mention the issue of the authority of the Book and Sunnah as a principality and origin. Finally, what is the reason for mentioning only the issue of the authority of ijma' and qiyas?

Answer: The author gives it from his statement 'but the usuli's engagement'. The summary is that the authority of the Quran and Sunnah is agreed upon and consensual for the entire Ummah of Muhammad, there is no disagreement in it, so usulis do not discuss it. In contrast, there is severe disagreement in the Ummah regarding the authority of ijma' and qiyas. Thus, al-Nazzam al-Mu'tazili and some Rafidis and Khawarij completely denied ijma'. Dawud al-Zahiri and his followers, and according to one narration Imam Ahmad, restricted ijma' to the Companions. Among the Shia, the Zaydis and Imamis only considered the ijma' of the family of the Prophet as valid. Similarly, the Zahiris denied the authority of qiyas. For this reason, usulis considered it necessary to establish the authority of ijma' and qiyas, because the severe disagreement and conflict in the authority of ijma' and qiyas caused disagreement and conflict in usuli issues, since the foundation of usuli issues is based on the wall of the authority of ijma' and qiyas. Therefore, specifically mentioning these two was needed, and since there is no disagreement regarding the Book and Sunnah, there is no great need to mention them.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an extended commentary on a statement from the matn (likely Muslim al-Thubut) concerning the classification of the discussion on the authority (hujjiyya) of ijma' (consensus) and qiyas (analogy). The author, al-Shaykh al-Hanafi, is addressing a dispute about whether the authority of these sources belongs to 'ilm al-kalam (theology) or usul al-fiqh (legal theory). The passage begins by noting that if qiyas is defined as the equality between the original and the branch due to a divine cause, then its authority becomes a necessary matter of religion (daruriyyat diniyya), not a theoretical issue of a particular science. Ibn al-Humam is cited as holding two views: that the authority of qiyas is a fiqh issue because qiyas is an act of the mujtahid, but also that it is not a matter of any science because it involves divine equality. The author dismisses this attribution as incorrect. He then asserts that the truth is that the authority of ijma' and qiyas is from kalam, just like the authority of the Quran and Sunnah, because belief (i'tiqad) is sought from it. Usulis engage with it only as a principium (mabda'). An objection is raised: if all proofs are from kalam, why do usulis only discuss the authority of ijma' and qiyas? The answer explains that the Quran and Sunnah are universally accepted, while there is significant disagreement about ijma' and qiyas from various groups (Mu'tazila, Zahiris, Khawarij, etc.). Therefore, usulis must establish their authority to build usul al-fiqh upon them.

Key Terms
حجیت (hujjiyya): Authority or probative value of a source of Shari'a (e.g., Quran, Sunnah, Ijma', Qiyas).
قیاس (qiyas): The equality between an original and a branch due to a cause from Allah; analogical reasoning in law.
اجماع (ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of the Ummah on a Shari'a ruling.
علم کلام ('ilm al-kalam): Theological science dealing with matters of belief, including the authority of religious proofs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do usulis discuss the authority of ijma' and qiyas but not the authority of the Quran and Sunnah in usul al-fiqh texts?
A) Because the Quran and Sunnah are not considered proofs by some groups
B) Because there is no disagreement among Muslims about the authority of the Quran and Sunnah
C) Because ijma' and qiyas are more foundational for usul al-fiqh
D) Because the Prophet prohibited discussing the authority of the Quran

Key Takeaway
The authority of ijma' and qiyas is a theological issue (kalam), but usulis discuss it because it is contested, unlike the universally accepted Quran and Sunnah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Proof for the External Existence of Absolute Essence
Presenting a proof for the existence of absolute essence in the external world

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proof for the external existence of absolute essence (al-mahiyya al-mutlaqa) and explain its importance for qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Absolute essence exists externally as the substrate of multiple individuations, proven by the similarity of water drops.

This passage presents a rational proof for the existence of absolute essence, a concept that grounds the validity of analogical reasoning (qiyas) in Hanafi usul. The author defends the external existence of absolute essence against those who hold that only individuals exist. Understanding this proof clarifies how universals are applied to particular cases in fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three considerations of essence
Note the three ways essence is considered: mixed with accidents (al-mahiyya al-mukhtalita), stripped of accidents (al-mahiyya al-mujarrada), and absolute essence (al-mahiyya al-mutlaqa). The first exists externally by consensus, the second does not, and the third is disputed.
2
Understand the disagreement
The author claims absolute essence exists externally as the substrate of multiple individuations. Opponents argue only individuals exist, and absolute essences are mere mental abstractions from simple essences (huwiyyat basita).
3
Follow the water drop proof (first formulation)
If absolute essence did not exist, each drop of water would have a separate reality (haliqa). But water drops are similar and composed of hyle, corporeal form, and specific form, which implies a common reality. Thus, the consequent is false, so absolute essence must exist.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) using the similarity of substances.
4
Follow the water drop proof (second formulation)
Each drop either comprises both essence and individuation, or only individuation. If only individuation, then there is a differentiator without commonality, and drops would be mutually separate—which they are not. Hence, both essence and individuation exist in each drop.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The existence of absolute essence supports the validity of qiyas in Hanafi usul. If absolute essence were only mental, the common illa in qiyas would lack external grounding, weakening analogical reasoning.

Source Text

(۲) الماحية المجردة عن العوارض، یعنی ماہیت کا اس کے عوارض سے خالی و عاری ہو کر اعتبار جس کو ماہیت مجردہ اور ماہیت بشرط لاشی " سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔
(۳) الماهية من حیث ھی ھی ، یعنی ماهیت کا عوارض کی مقارنت با عوارض کے تجرد ہر دو سے صرف نظر کر کے اعتبار، جس کو ماہیت مطلقہ ، ماہیت بلا شر ط شئی سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔
مندرجہ بالا تینوں اعتبارات میں سے ماہیت باعتبار اول ( ماہیت مخلوطه ) بالا تفاق خارج میں موجود ہے۔ اور ماہیت باعتبار ثانی (ماہیت مجردہ) بالاتفاق خارج میں نہیں پائی جاتی ۔ رہے ماهیت باعتبار ثالث ( ماہیت مطلقہ ) تو اسکے موجود ہونے نہ ہونے میں مناطقہ کا اختلاف ہے۔ جسکو وہ حضرات کلی طبعی سے بھی یاد کرتے ہیں۔
محققین مناطقہ ماہیت مطلقہ کو خارج میں موجود مانتے ہیں اور مائن کا بھی یہی نظریہ ہے اس لئے کہا ” الماهية المطلقة موجودة"
مصنف کا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ ماہیت مطلقہ، یا ماهیت بلا شر ط شئی بعینہ اشخاص کے وجود کے ساتھ موجود ہے بایں طور کہ اس ماہیت پرشی کا تشخص عارض ہوتا ہے اور ماہیت تشخص کا معروض ہو کر پائی جاتی ہے البتہ اس ماهیت پر تشخصات کثیرہ عارض ہوتے ہیں تو ماھیت اشخاص متعددہ ہو جاتی ہے اور وجودات متکثرہ کے ساتھ پائی جاتی ہے، الغرض خارج میں دو چیز میں پائی جاتی ہیں ایک حقیقت مطلقہ، اور دوسرے اشخاص یعنی وہ حقیقت جو تشخصات متعددہ کا معروض ہوتی ہے تا ہم دونوں وجود خارجی کے اعتبار سے متحد ہوتے ہیں البتہ ان دونوں میں سے ایک کا تعقل دوسرے کے بغیر لحاظ ذہن میں دو اعتبار سے ہو سکتا ہے۔ چنانچہ جب اس حقیقت کو ظرف میں اشخاص سے قطع نظر کر کے تعقل کیا جائے تو یہی حقیقت کلیت، اشتراک، اور عموم و اطلاق وغیرھا اوصاف سے ذھنا متصف ہوتی ہے اس لئے کہ کہ ان اوصاف کے ساتھ جو ماهیت متصف ہوتی ہے اس کا ظرف عروض واتصاف خاص وجہ ذہنی ہے کیونکہ ماہیت ان اوصاف کے ساتھ خارج میں متصف نہیں ہو سکتی، چونکہ وجود خارجی تشخص کا مساوق و ملا زم ہوتا ہے اور مساوقیت تشخص ان اوصاف کے منافی ومبائن ہے چنانچہ کلیت ، اشتراک اور عموم و اطلاق وغیر ہ اوصاف اور تشخص کے مابین منافات ظاہر ہے یہ مصنف اور ان کے ہم خیال علماء کا نظریہ ہے۔
اس کے برعکس کچھ علما فن کا یہ نظر یہ ہے کہ ماہیت مطلقہ خارج میں نہیں پائی جاتی ، خارج میں صرف اور صرف اشخاص موجود ہوتے ہیں جس کو ہو یت بسیطہ کہتے ہیں جن سے طبائع کلیہ عقلاً منتزع کئے جاتے ہیں اور یہ ھو یات بسیطہ بذات خود متمیز و تشخص ہوتے ہیں چونکہ تشخصات بسیطہ ان ذوات بسیطہ سے عبارت ہے جو کسی ایسی ایک حقیقت میں مشترک نہ ہوں جو حقیقت کہ تشخصات کثیر نا معروض ہو مصنف اس خیال کو غلط قرار دیتے ہوئے کہتے ہیں ' والا لكان لكل قطرة من الماء حقيقة علیحدة، یعنی اگر ماہیت مطلقہ خارج میں موجود نہ ہوگی تو پانی کے ہر ہر قطرہ کے لئے علیحدہ علیحدہ حقیقت ہو جائے گی اور تالی باطل ہے کیونکہ جواہر کا تماثل اور حقیقت میں متحد ہونا ثابت شدہ امر ہے پس تماثل جواہر اسی تقدیر پرممکن ہے جب خارج میں ماھیت مطلقہ کا وجود مانا جائے ۔ دلیل کا خلاصہ : ماهیت مطلقہ کے موجود ہونے پر مصنف کی اس دلیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جسم بسیط جیسے "پانی کے افراد بلاشبہ خارج میں موجود ہیں اب سوال یہ ہے کہ پانی کے ان افراد کے درمیان کوئی حقیقت مشتر کہ پائی جاتی ہے یا نہیں ، بصورت اثبات حقیقت مطلقہ کا وجود ثابت ہے۔ اور بصورت نفی سوال یہ ہے کہ پانی کے جملہ افراد میں سے ہر ہر فرد میں ھیولی ، صورت جسمیہ اور پانی کی صورت نوعیہ موجود ہوگی یا نہیں، اگر موجود ہوگی تو افراد ماء کے ہر فرد میں حقیقت ماء کا وجود ہوگا اس لئے کہ حقیقت عبارت ہے اس جسم سے جو ھیولی صورت جسمیہ اور نوعیہ سے مرکب ہو۔ اور اگر پانی کے افراد میں سے کسی فرد میں ھیوئی صورت جسمیہ و نوعیہ نہیں پائی جارہی ہے تو اس وقت لازم آئے گا کہ افراد ماء کا کوئی فرد قابل قسمت، صح لفرض ابعاد ثلثہ نہ ہوگا اور نہ ہی آثار خارجیہ کا قابل ہوگا کہ صورت جسمیہ ونوعیہ کا العدم فرض کر لیا گیا، والملازم صریح البطلان فا الملز وم مثلہ ۔ دلیل کی دوسری تقریر :۔ بھی کی جاتی ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ بلاشبہ قطرات ماء خارج میں موجود ہیں پس ان قطرات میں سے ہر قطرہ یا تو ماهیت و شخص دونوں پر مشتمل ہوگا یا صرف تشخص پر مشتمل ہوگا بر تقدیر اول مطلوب ثابت ، اور بر تقدیر ثانی جہاں یہ لازم آتا ہے کہ مابہ الاشتراک کے بغیر ما بہ الامتیاز موجود ہے وہیں پر پانی کے ہر قطرہ کا آپس میں ایک دوسرے کے مبائن ہونا لازم آئے گا اسلئے کہ تشخصات بذا تھا متبائن ہوتے ہیں جبکہ پانی کے ہر قطرہ کا ایک دوسرے کے مبائن ہونا ظاہر
(2) The essence stripped of accidents: i.e., considering the essence free and devoid of its accidents, which they call essence abstracted and essence with the condition of nothing. (3) The essence as such: i.e., considering the essence disregarding both the accompaniment of accidents and the stripping of accidents, which they call absolute essence and essence without any condition. Among the three considerations above, essence in the first sense (mixed essence) exists externally by consensus. Essence in the second sense (abstracted essence) does not exist externally by consensus. As for essence in the third sense (absolute essence), there is disagreement among the philosophers regarding its existence or non-existence – they also refer to it as natural universal. The verifiers among the philosophers hold that absolute essence exists externally, and the Manians likewise hold this view, so it is said: 'The absolute essence exists.' The author's claim is that absolute essence, or essence without condition, exists exactly with the existence of individuals, in such a way that individuation (tashakhkhus) occurs to that essence and the essence is found as the substrate of individuation. However, multiple individuations occur to it, so the essence becomes multiple individuals and is found with multiple existences. In short, two things are found externally: one is absolute reality, and the other is individuals – that is, the reality that is the substrate of multiple individuations. Nevertheless, both are united in terms of external existence, but one of them can be intellectually conceived without the other in two respects. Thus, when this reality is conceived in the mind disregarding individuals, it is mentally described with predicates like universality, commonality, generality, absoluteness, etc. This is because the locus of occurrence and description for these predicates is the specific mental aspect, since essence cannot be described with these predicates externally. Because external existence is concomitant and inseparable from individuation, and the concomitance of individuation is contrary and opposite to these predicates. Hence, the incompatibility between universality, commonality, generality, etc., and individuation is evident. This is the view of the author and like-minded scholars. In contrast, some scholars of the discipline hold that absolute essence is not found externally; externally only individuals exist, which they call simple essences (huwiyyat basita), from which universal natures are intellectually abstracted. These simple essences are in themselves distinguished and individuated, because simple individuations consist of those simple essences that do not share in a single reality that is the substrate of multiple individuations. The author rejects this view and says: 'Otherwise, each drop of water would have a separate reality.' That is, if absolute essence did not exist externally, then every single drop of water would have a separate reality. The consequent is false because the similarity (tamathul) of substances and their unity in reality is an established matter. Therefore, the similarity of substances is only possible if the existence of absolute essence is affirmed externally. Summary of the proof: The gist of the author's proof for the existence of absolute essence is that the individuals of a simple body like water undoubtedly exist externally. The question is: Is there a common reality among these individuals of water or not? If affirmed, then the existence of absolute reality is proven. If denied, the question is: Does every individual of water have hyle (hayula), corporeal form (sura jismiyya), and the specific form of water (sura naw'iyya) or not? If they exist, then the reality of water exists in every individual because reality is defined as a body composed of hyle, corporeal form, and specific form. If in any individual these three are not found, then it would follow that no individual of water is divisible, nor can three dimensions be assumed, nor can it be receptive to external effects, since corporeal and specific forms are assumed absent. The consequent is clearly false, so the antecedent is likewise. The second exposition of the proof: Another formulation is that without doubt drops of water exist externally. Each drop either comprises both essence and individuation, or comprises only individuation. In the first case, the desired conclusion is proven. In the second case, it necessarily follows that the differentiator exists without the commonality, and also that every drop of water is mutually separate from another, because individuations are mutually separate in themselves, yet it is evident that drops of water are not mutually separate.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a philosophical argument within usul al-fiqh concerning the existence of the 'absolute essence' (al-mahiyya al-mutlaqa) in the external world. The author presents three ways of considering essence: mixed with accidents (found externally by consensus), stripped of accidents (not found externally by consensus), and absolute essence – which is the subject of dispute. The author, following the verifiers among the philosophers (muhaqqiqun), asserts that absolute essence exists externally, serving as the substrate for multiple individuations. The author then engages with an opposing view that denies external existence of absolute essence, claiming only individuals exist. To refute this, the author provides a proof using the example of water drops. The argument is based on the similarity of water drops: if there were no common essence, each drop would have a distinct reality, contradicting observed similarity. The proof is presented in two ways: first, by analyzing the composition of water (hyle, corporeal form, specific form) and showing that denial leads to absurdity; second, by considering that each drop must have both essence and individuation, or else drops would be mutually separate, which they are not. This establishes the existence of absolute essence as a necessary condition for the similarity of substances. The passage illustrates the use of rational proof (dalil aqli) in usul discussions.

Key Terms
الماهية المطلقة (al-māhiyya al-muṭlaqa): The essence considered without any condition, i.e., absolute essence that is the substrate of multiple individuations and exists externally according to the author.
تشخص (tashakhkhuṣ): Individuation; the particularization that distinguishes one existing individual from another.
كلي طبيعي (kullī ṭabīʿī): Natural universal; the universal that exists in the external world as a common reality in multiple individuals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what would happen if absolute essence did not exist externally, using the example of water drops?
A) Water drops would be identical.
B) Each drop of water would have a separate reality.
C) Water drops would cease to exist.
D) The concept of water would become meaningless.

Key Takeaway
The external existence of absolute essence is proven by rational necessity, as it explains the similarity of individuals and grounds valid qiyas.

The Philosophical Proof for Absolute Essence: Atomism and Euclidean Geometry
Introducing a philosophical proof with disclaimer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the author introduces a philosophical proof for absolute essence and identify the key concepts (indivisible atom, Euclidean propositions) used.

Core Idea
The author offers a rational proof for absolute essence but disclaims it as contrary to Islamic law, using atomism and geometry.

This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut begins a new argument for the existence of mahiyyah mutlaqah, shifting from a failed proof based on tamathul to a philosophical one. The author signals this by saying 'I say in the manner of philosophy' and notes that this proof contradicts Islamic law, so it is not his actual belief. To follow the argument, you must understand the indivisible atom (juz' alladhi la yatajazzi) and two Euclidean propositions: the triangle inequality (shakl himari) and the Pythagorean theorem (shakl 'arusi). The passage is incomplete, but the groundwork is laid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context and disclaimer
The previous proof failed. The author now presents a proof 'in the manner of philosophy' and explicitly says it contradicts Islamic law, so it is not his personal view. This frames the entire argument as hypothetical.
The disclaimer protects the author from being accused of unbelief.
2
Define the indivisible atom
The 'juz' alladhi la yatajazzi' is a particle that cannot be divided in reality or in the mind. Mutakallimun accept it; philosophers reject it. Bodies are composed of these atoms.
This is a key premise of the proof.
3
Understand the geometric tools
Two Euclidean propositions are cited: shakl himari (triangle inequality: sum of two sides > third side) and shakl 'arusi (Pythagorean theorem). These will be used to derive a contradiction about atom composition.
The names 'donkey' and 'bride' are traditional.
4
Infer the argument structure (incomplete)
The passage cuts off, but the likely argument is: if a right triangle's legs are composed of an integer number of atoms, then the hypotenuse would not be an integer length (due to Pythagorean theorem), making it impossible to have commensurate sides under atomism. This refutes atomism and supports a non-material essence.
The full proof is on subsequent pages.
5
Note the lesson for usul al-fiqh
Using rational proofs that contradict revelation is rejected in Hanafi usul. The author's disclaimer shows that such arguments are not to be taken as authoritative.
This illustrates the priority of naqli over aqli when they conflict.

His statement: 'I say in the manner of philosophy (ḥikmah). For if the part (juz') were true, etc.' The proof for the existence of absolute essence in the external world was dependent on the proof of tamathul among jawahir. And whether one intends union in reality or sharing in descriptions from tamathul of jawahir, in either case the proof does not provide the proof of absolute essence. Therefore, the author, while proving tamathul among jawahir upon the existence of absolute essence, mentions a proof that is not subject to criticism. So he said: 'I say in the manner of philosophy.' The phrase 'in the manner of philosophy' indicates that this proof contradicts Islamic law, so it is not my own opinion; my discourse is based on a philosophical manner. To understand the author's proof, it is necessary to keep in mind several points:
(1) In the text, 'al-juz'' means the indivisible atom (juz' alladhi lā yatajazzā).
(2) The indivisible atom is that which does not accept division at all, neither by cutting nor by estimation or assumption. Bodies are composed of it. According to the mutakallimun, the indivisible atom is true and established, while philosophers (hukamā') consider it false; for them, body is composed of matter (hayūlā) and form (sūrah).
(3) Right angle: A straight line drawn perpendicular to a vertical line forms a right angle. According to modern mathematics, it is 90 degrees. Its shape is [diagram].
(4) Hypotenuse (watar): The third line of a triangle that meets the two sides is called the hypotenuse. Each line of the triangle is called a side (ḍil'). Its shape is [diagram].
If we assume each side is two parts, then both sides together will be three parts instead of four, because one part is shared between the two sides. The shape of the donkey (shakl ḥimārī): The 20th proposition of the first book of Euclid's Elements, which states that two sides of a triangle together are greater than the third side. For example, if one side is two parts, then two sides together will be greater than the third, i.e., three parts. Thus the hypotenuse, which is the third line, will be smaller than their sum of three parts. Otherwise, the claim of the shape would be invalid. The shape of the bride (shakl 'arūsī): The 47th proposition of the first book of Euclid's Elements, which states that in every right-angled triangle, the square of the hypotenuse equals the sum of the squares of the two sides containing the right angle. The conclusion is that...

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of a new proof for the existence of absolute essence based on the concept of the indivisible atom and geometric principles. The author notes that the previous proof was dependent on tamathul and failed. So he presents a new proof 'in the manner of philosophy' (i.e., using rational arguments, not necessarily conforming to Islamic teachings). He then defines key terms:
- The indivisible atom (juz' alladhi la yatajazzi) is a fundamental particle that cannot be divided, accepted by mutakallimun but rejected by philosophers who see body as composed of matter and form.
- Geometric concepts: right angle, hypotenuse, and two Euclidean propositions: the triangle inequality (shakl himari) and the Pythagorean theorem (shakl 'arusi). These are used to argue about the composition of the triangle from atoms. The argument seems to be that if sides of a right triangle are composed of an integer number of atoms, then the hypotenuse would not be an integer number of atoms, leading to a contradiction unless indivisible atoms are false. This supports the existence of absolute essence beyond the material. However, the passage is cut off, so the full argument is not given. The author's note that this contradicts Islamic law suggests that this philosophical argument is hypothetical, not his actual belief.
This is a classic debate in kalam: whether the universe is composed of indivisible atoms or continuous matter, and its implications for theology.

Key Terms
جزء الذي لا يتجزي (juz' alladhi la yatajazzi): The indivisible atom that does not accept division at all, from which bodies are composed.
طور الحكمة (tawr al-hikmah): The manner of philosophy, i.e., rational argument not necessarily based on revelation.
شكل حمارى (shakl himari): The 20th proposition of Euclid's Elements: triangle inequality.
شكل عروسى (shakl 'arusi): The 47th proposition of Euclid's Elements: Pythagorean theorem.

Key Takeaway
The author introduces a rational proof for absolute essence using atomism and geometry but explicitly disclaims it as contrary to Islamic law, illustrating the Hanafi principle that revealed evidence takes precedence over philosophical reasoning.

The Hanafi Scope of Dalil: Broad vs. Restricted Definitions
Comparing logical and restricted definitions of proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the broad (logician's) and restricted (self-necessity) definitions of dalil and explain why Hanafi usul accepts istiqra and tamthil as valid proofs.

Core Idea
Dalil in Hanafi usul is broader than qiyas: istiqra and tamthil are accepted proofs.

In this passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut, the commentator compares two definitions of 'dalil' (proof). The first, adopted by logicians, is broad and encompasses multiple forms of reasoning. The second adds restrictions of self-necessity, limiting proof to qiyas alone. For the Hanafi usuli, understanding this distinction is crucial because it shapes which methods of legal reasoning are considered authoritative in deriving rulings from the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate in the text where the first definition is given (logicians: qawlan yakunu 'anhu qawl akhar) and where the second is introduced (qad yuqalu yastalzimu li-dhatihi qawl akhar).
The first definition is general; the second is specific.
2
Understand the scope of the first definition
Recognize that the first definition covers qiyas, istiqra, tamthil, and even the five arts. The key is that it requires only that two statements produce a third, regardless of certainty.
Luzum can be bayyin or ghayr bayyin.
3
Apply the first definition to empirical examples
Work through the examples in the text: istiqra from multiple animal observations to a universal rule, and tamthil from wine to nabidh via the 'illa of intoxication.
These show how the broad definition accommodates inductive and analogical reasoning.
4
Analyze the second definition's restrictions
The second definition adds 'yastalzimu li-dhatihi' (necessarily implies by itself). This restricts proof to qiyas only, and even excludes qiyas al-musawat because it requires an external premise.
According to the author, this definition is too narrow and not approved.
5
Determine the Hanafi preference
The commentator signals disapproval by introducing the second definition with 'qad yuqala' (it is said), indicating it is weak. Hanafi usul follows the broader definition to include istiqra and tamthil as valid proofs.
This aligns with the Hanafi method of deriving rulings from inductive reading of texts and analogical extension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله " وهو يتناول الاستقراء والتمثيل ۔ اس کا قول ھو کی ضمیر "ما" کی طرف راجع ہے معنی یہ ہے کہ منطقی نے دلیل کی تعریف میں جو کہا ہے وہ دلیل کے تینوں اقسام قیاس استقراء اور تمثیل کو شامل ہے بلکہ صناعات خمسہ جدل خطاب اور مغالطہ وغیرہ کو بھی عام ہے اس لئے کہ منطقی کا یہ کہنا کہ قولین سے قول آخر کا حصول ہو ، عام کہ یہ حصول لزوم بین کے طور پر ہو یا غیر بین کے طور پر، چنانچہ استقراء تمثیل و غیر با کی تعریف سے ظاہر ہے کہ ان میں سے ہر ایک ایسے قولین کی طرف راجع ہے جن دونوں کے مرکب سے قول آخر حاصل ہوتا ہے۔ چونکہ استقراء کہتے ہیں حکم کلی کے اثبات کے لئے جزئیات کثیرہ کے تتبع کرنے کو جیسے الانسان يتحرك فكه الاسفل عند المضغ

والفرس يتحرك فكه الاسفل عند ا لمضغ كذالك الحماء والغنم... ۔ اس قول سے
قول آخر كل حيوان يتحرك فكه الاسفل عند المضع کا حکم لگانا درست ہے۔ تمثیل فرع واصل یا مقیس و مقیس علیہ کے درمیان علت حکم میں مساوات ثابت کرنے کو کہتے ہیں اس تعریف پر قولان یکون عند قول آخر کا صدق ہوتا ہے مثلا کہا جائے الخمر حرام للاسكار والنبيذ يوجد فيه الاسكار ، اس دو قول سے ثابت ہوتا ہے النبیذ حرام، یعنی نبیذ حرام ہے اس واسطے کہ وہ چیز جو علت حکم میں شئی کے مساوی ہوتی ہے تو اس شئی مساوی (مقیس ) کا حکم نفس شئی (مقیس علیہ ) کا حکم ہوتا ہے۔
قوله. وقد يقال يستلزم لذاته قولا آخر فيختص بالقياس " اس عبارت سے دلیل کی ایک دوسری تعریف ذکر کر رہے ہیں ، دلیل کی تعریف مذکور اور اس تعریف میں عام و خاص مطلق کی نسبت ہے تعریف اول عام اور تعریف دوم خاص ہے کہ اول قیاس واستقراء اور تمثیل وغیرھا سب کو شامل ہے جبکہ دوم صرف قیاس کے ساتھ خاص ہے پھر تعریف اول میں قولین سے قول آخر کا علم و حصول یقینی نہیں ہے بلکہ ظنی ہے اور تعریف دوم میں قولین سے قول آخر کا علم یقینی ولازمی ہے۔ دونوں تعریف میں تیسرا فرق یہ ہے کہ اول میں قولین سے مطلوب کا علم لذاتہ ضروری نہیں اور دوم کے مطابق لذاتہ بلا واسطہ شئی ضروری ہوتا ہے۔ مصنف کے نزدیک دلیل کی یہ تعریف نا پسندیدہ ہے اس لئے قدیقال سے ذکر کر کے اس کے ضعف کی طرف اشارہ کیا ، وجہ ضعف یہ ہیکہ اس تعریف کی بنا پر استقرا تمثیل اور قیاس المساوات وغیرہ افراد دلیل سے خارج ہوئے جاتے ہیں فرق مذکور سے ظاہر ہے کہ اس تعریف میں یستلزم کی قید استقراء اور تمثیل کو نکالنے کے لئے ہے کیونکہ استقراء و تمثیل میں شئی آخر کا لزوم ضروری نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور لذاتہ کی قید سے اس دلیل کو نکالنا ہے جو مقدمہ غیر لازمہ کے واسطہ سے نتیجہ دیتی ہے جیسا کہ قیاس مساوات میں ہوتا ہے چنانچہ مثا' مادی جاتی ہے کہ امساوِ لِب، وب مساولج، ينتج أمساولج اس مثال میں نتیجہ کا لزوم لذا تہ نہیں ہے بلکہ ایک مقدمہ خارجیہ کے واسطہ سے ہے اور مقدمہ خارجیہ یہ ہے ” مساوی المساوی مساوی شارح خیر آبادی نے کہا ہے کہ اس تعریف میں استلزام اور لذاتہ کی قید میں ایک ہی قید ہے جو ایسی دلیلوں کے
Ashraf al-Nu'ut Sharh Muslim al-Thubut. 142. The required [conclusion] consists of the predicate and the middle term, so the author said: 'Thus the two premises are necessary.' His statement: 'From here, the logician said: It is two statements from which another statement [is derived]...' With this expression, the matan is presenting support for his previous claim. His claim was that for the production (intaj) of a proof, three things or two premises are necessary. With his statement 'there must be a middle term' he indicated the proof, and with his statement 'From here, the logician said' he presented support that for this reason, for the production of a proof, two premises are necessary. The logicians have defined proof as that which actually consists of two premises, and thus they defined it as: 'It is two statements from which another statement is obtained.' That is, proof is two propositions from which another proposition is derived. It should be clear that in the definition, 'statement' (qawl) means 'proposition' (qadiyya), although the term 'statement' applies to restrictive compounds, non-restrictive, incomplete, complete, informative, and performative, etc., but in the context of definition, by 'statement' is meant a complete informative compound, because taking a general expression and intending a specific meaning is common and widespread. For this reason, 'statement' was interpreted as 'proposition', since the proof brings about the verification of the required and intended [conclusion]. In his statement 'from which' (yakunu 'anhu), the pronoun refers back to the aforementioned 'two statements' (qawlan) by way of interpretation, and the pronoun is singular to indicate the aspect of affirmation: after the form of productive combination occurs, 'the two statements become a single statement.' And what was said that from the combination of two statements another statement is derived, its meaning is that from the combination of two statements, confirmation (tasdiq) is attached. His statement: 'And it encompasses induction (istiqra) and analogy (tamthil).' The pronoun 'hu' in his statement 'huwa' refers back to 'ma' [the definition]. The meaning is that what the logician said in the definition of proof includes all three types of proof: qiyas, istiqra, and tamthil, indeed it also includes the five arts: jadal, khitab, and mughalata, etc. This is because the logician's saying that from two statements a third statement is obtained is general, whether this obtaining is in the form of evident necessity (luzum bayyin) or non-evident necessity. Thus, from the definition of istiqra, tamthil, etc., it is clear that each of them goes back to two statements from whose combination a third statement is obtained. For example: istiqra is the investigation of many particulars to establish a universal rule, such as: 'Man moves his lower jaw when chewing, the horse moves his lower jaw when chewing, likewise the donkey and the sheep...' from this statement, it is valid to establish the rule: 'Every animal moves its lower jaw when chewing.' Tamthil is to establish equality between a branch and root (or between the object of analogy and the analogue) in the effective cause of the ruling. Under this definition, 'two statements from which another statement is obtained' applies. For example, it is said: 'Wine is prohibited because it intoxicates, and nabidh contains intoxication.' From these two statements it is established: 'Nabidh is prohibited.' That is, nabidh is prohibited because the thing that is equal to another thing in the effective cause of the ruling, the ruling of that equal thing (maqis) is the ruling of the thing itself (maqis 'alayh). His statement: 'And it is said: It necessarily implies (yastalzimu) by itself (li-dhatihi) another statement, so it is specific to qiyas.' With this expression, he mentions another definition of proof. The relationship between the mentioned definition and this definition is that of general and specific in an absolute sense: the first definition is general and the second is specific, because the first includes qiyas, istiqra, tamthil, etc., all of them, while the second is specific only to qiyas. Then, in the first definition, knowledge and obtaining of another statement from the two statements is not certain but rather conjectural, while in the second definition, knowledge of another statement from the two statements is certain and necessary. A third difference between the two definitions is that in the first, knowledge of the required from the two statements is not necessary by themselves, but according to the second, it is necessary by themselves without an intermediary. According to the author, this definition of proof is not approved, so by mentioning it with 'it is said' (qad yuqalu) he indicated its weakness. The reason for its weakness is that based on this definition, istiqra, tamthil, and qiyas al-musawat, etc., are excluded from the individuals of proof. From the mentioned difference it is clear that the restriction 'yastalzimu' in this definition is to exclude istiqra and tamthil because in istiqra and tamthil the necessity of another thing is not necessary. And the restriction 'li-dhatihi' is to exclude that proof which produces a conclusion through a non-essential premise, as occurs in qiyas al-musawat. For example, the example is given: 'A is equal to B, and B is equal to C, therefore A is equal to C.' In this example, the conclusion's necessity is not by itself but rather through an external premise, and the external premise is: 'That which is equal to the equal is equal.' The commentator Khayrabadi said that in this definition, the two restrictions 'yastalzimu' and 'li-dhatihi' are one and the same restriction, which excludes such proofs...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Muslim al-Thubut discusses the definition of 'dalil' (proof) as understood by logicians and its application in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins by noting that the matan (Muslim al-Thubut) previously mentioned that for a proof to produce a conclusion (intaj), three components are needed: two premises and a middle term. To support this, the matan quotes the logicians' definition: 'Proof is two statements from which another statement is derived.' The commentator explains that in this definition, 'statement' (qawl) means proposition (qadiyya), specifically a complete informative proposition, even though the word 'qawl' has wider applications. The pronoun in 'from which' (yakunu 'anhu) refers to the two statements, and the singular pronoun indicates that the two statements become a single logical unit after their productive combination. The commentator then notes that the logician's definition covers all types of reasoning: syllogism (qiyas), induction (istiqra), and analogy (tamthil), as well as the five arts of logic (dialectic, rhetoric, sophistry, etc.) because the derivation of a third statement from two statements can be either evident or non-evident. He provides examples: for istiqra, observing that humans, horses, donkeys, etc., move their jaws when chewing leads to the generalization 'All animals move their jaws when chewing.' For tamthil, drawing an analogy between wine (khamr) and nabidh (date-wine) based on the common effective cause ('illa) of intoxication yields the ruling that nabidh is also prohibited. The passage then introduces a second, more restrictive definition: 'Proof is that which necessarily implies by itself another statement, so it is specific to qiyas.' The commentator points out that this definition is narrower—it excludes istiqra and tamthil because they do not give certain, self-evident necessity, and it also excludes qiyas al-musawat (analogy of equality) because the conclusion there requires an external premise (e.g., 'Things equal to the same thing are equal'). The author of the sharh (Mulla Nizam al-Din?) appears to favor the broader definition, as he signals disapproval of the narrow definition by using the phrase 'it is said' (qad yuqalu) and explaining its weaknesses. This discussion is important for Hanafi usul because it clarifies how different forms of reasoning are treated in legal argumentation, especially the role of istiqra' (induction) and tamthil (analogy) in deriving rulings, while emphasizing that the definitive proof (qiyas jali) is the strongest form.

Key Terms
الدليل (al-dalil): Two statements from which another statement is derived; a proof that establishes a conclusion
الاستقراء (al-istiqra): Tracing many particulars to establish a universal rule
التمثيل (al-tamthil): Establishing equality between a branch (far') and a root (asl) in the effective cause (illa) of a ruling
القياس (al-qiyas): Syllogism; a form of proof where the conclusion follows necessarily from the premises
اللزوم (al-luzum): Necessary implication; the conclusion must follow from the premises

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why does the second definition (with 'yastalzimu li-dhatihi') exclude istiqra and tamthil?
A) Because they do not involve two premises
B) Because they do not produce certain, self-necessary implication
C) Because they are not used by logicians
D) Because they are based on observation

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school adopts a broad definition of dalil that includes qiyas, istiqra, and tamthil, in contrast to narrow definitions that restrict proof to self-necessary syllogism.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
First Close Form of Qiyas: Affirmative Minor and Universal Major
Stating and explaining the first of the five forms of qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid qiyas in the first close form and apply the Hanafi rule for subsuming a negative minor.

Core Idea
For qiyas to be productive by itself, the minor must be affirmative and the major universal.

The first close form of qiyas, as defined in Muslim al-Thubut, is the most direct syllogistic structure in Hanafi usul. Its power lies in its self-sufficiency: when the premises are correctly formed, the conclusion follows necessarily. This lesson dissects the two indispensable conditions—affirmative minor and universal major—and explains how to handle a negative minor through reinterpretation as an affirmative with a negative predicate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first close form
The source states that the first form is: know the ruling for every individual of a thing, then know that thing exists (wholly or partially) in another. Then the ruling necessarily applies to that other.
This is a syllogism with a universal major and an affirmative minor.
2
Extract the two conditions
The text explicitly requires 'affirmation of the minor' (ایجاب صغری) and 'universality of the major' (کلیت کبری). Without both, the qiyas is not productive by itself.
These are the key conditions for a self-sufficient qiyas.
3
Understand the critique of al-Tahrir
Some argue that if the extremes of the major are coextensive (equal), the minor need not be affirmative. The author rejects this, saying such a qiyas is not productive 'by itself' (li dhatihi).
Equal extremes mean the major is effectively a definition, not a universal quantification that yields new knowledge.
4
Address the objection of a negative minor
An objection: 'A is not B, and every not-B is C' seems to work with a negative minor. The answer: the major's predicate 'not-B' is considered with its affirmative existence in mind. The minor must be reinterpreted as 'A is (not-B)' i.e., an affirmative with a negative predicate.
This preserves the affirmative minor condition by converting a negative statement into an affirmative one with a negated predicate.
5
Apply the reinterpretation rule
In practice, if the minor appears negative, transform it into a positive proposition where the predicate is negated. For example, 'Zaid is not seeing' becomes 'Zaid is (not-seeing)' i.e., 'Zaid is blind'. Then it can be subsumed under a universal major about 'not-seeing'.
This technique allows qiyas to proceed without violating the affirmative minor condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم :- وله خمس صور قريبة الاولى ان يعلم حكم لكل افراد شئى ثم يعلم بثوته للآخر كلا او بعضاً فيلزم ثبوت ذالك الحكم للآخر کذالک بالضرورة فلابد من ايجاب الصغرى وكلية الكبرى ومافى التحرير في طرفى الكبرى فليس بشئى لانه ليس لذاته وأورد أليس ب وكل ماليس ب ج والجواب أن السلب من حيث هو هو رفع محض وعقد الوضع فى الكبرى لا يخلو من ملاحظة ثبوت فان لاحظته في الصغرى فلاسلب بل ايجاب سلب والافلا اندراج :ترجمہ : ۔ اور قیاس کی پانچ قریبی صورتیں ہیں پہلی صورت یہ ہے کہ کسی شئی کے ہر ہر فرد کا حکم معلوم کر لیا جائے پھر اس شئی کا ثبوت دوسری شئی کے لئے کل یا بعضاً معلوم ہو جائے پس اسطرح اس حکم کا ثبوت دوسرے کے لئے ایسا ہی بالضرورة لازم ہوگا اس لئے اس میں ایجاب صغریٰ اور کلیت کبری کی شرط ضروری ہے۔ اور وہ جو تحریر میں ہے کہ کبری کے دونوں طرف مساوی ہونے کی صورت میں( ایجاب صغری کی شرط ضروری نہیں ) تو وہ بلاوجہ کی بات ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں منتج ہونا لذا تہ نہیں ہے اور اکیس ب و کل مالیس ب ج سے اعتراض کیا گیا جواب یہ ہے کہ سب بحیثیت سلب رفع محض کا نام ہے اور کبری میں عقد وضع لحاظ ثبوت سے خالی نہیں لہذا اس ثبوت کا لحاظ اگر صغری میں کر لیا جائے تو صغری سالبہ نہیں رہ جائے گا بلکہ موجب سالبتہ الحمول ہو جائے گا اور اگر صغریٰ میں اس ثبوت کا لحاظ نہ کیا جائے تو مندرج نہیں ہوگا۔
Matn: 'And it has five close forms. The first: that the ruling for every individual of a thing is known, then its existence for another in whole or part is known, so necessarily the establishment of that ruling for the other follows in like manner. Therefore, the affirmation of the minor premise and the universality of the major are necessary. And what is in al-Tahrir regarding the two extremes of the major being equal is nothing, because it is not by itself. And the objection is raised: 'A is not B, and every not-B is C' — the answer is that negation, as such, is pure removal, and the affirmative construction in the major is not devoid of considering existence. If you consider that existence in the minor, then it is not a negation but an affirmative with a negative predicate; otherwise, it would not be subsumed.' Translation: 'And qiyas has five close forms. The first form is that the ruling for every individual of a thing is determined, then the existence of that thing for another is known wholly or partially. Thus, the establishment of that ruling for the other will necessarily follow. Therefore, in it, the condition of affirming the minor premise and the universality of the major is necessary. And what is in al-Tahrir that when both extremes of the major are equal, the condition of affirming the minor is not necessary — that is baseless. Because in that case, being productive is not by itself. And the objection is raised: 'A is not B, and every not-B is C' — the answer is that negation, as such, is pure removal, and the affirmative construction in the major is not devoid of considering existence. If you consider that existence in the minor, then the minor will not remain a negation but becomes an affirmative with a negative predicate. And if you do not consider that existence in the minor, it will not be subsumed.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut presents the first of five 'close forms' (suwar qaribah) of qiyas as mentioned in the matn of Muslim al-Thubut. The first form describes a syllogism where the universal major premise states that every individual of something has a certain ruling, and the minor premise establishes that the thing (or its existence) applies to another entity. The conclusion then necessarily applies the ruling to that entity. The commentary emphasizes that for this to work, the minor must be affirmative (not negative) and the major must be universal (kulliyyah). The author then critiques a view from al-Tahrir that when the two extremes of the major are coextensive (equals), the condition of affirming the minor is unnecessary. The commentator argues that such a qiyas would not be productive 'by itself' (li dhatihi). A specific objection is addressed: if the minor is negative ('A is not B') and the major is 'every not-B is C', then the minor must be reinterpreted as an affirmative with a negative predicate (موجب سالبتہ الحمول) to be subsumed under the major. The discussion shows the technical precision of Hanafi logic in ensuring that the syllogism yields a necessary conclusion.

Key Terms
صغری (sughra): The minor premise in a syllogism; must be affirmative for the qiyas to be productive by itself.
کبری (kubra): The major premise in a syllogism; must be universal (kulliyyah) for necessary entailment.
موجب سالبتہ الحمول (mujib salibat al-mahmul): An affirmative proposition with a negative predicate, e.g., 'Zaid is not-seeing' meaning 'Zaid is blind'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What condition does the commentary say is necessary for the first form of qiyas to be productive by itself?
A) The minor premise must be negative and the major particular.
B) The minor premise must be affirmative and the major universal.
C) The major must have equal extremes.
D) The conclusion must be the same as the minor.

Key Takeaway
The first close form of qiyas requires an affirmative minor premise and a universal major premise to produce a necessary conclusion by itself.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
