Qiyas Istithna'i: The Exceptive Syllogism in Hanafi Usul
Defines and explains the exceptive syllogism with conditions and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the structure of qiyas istithna'i, distinguish between conjunctive and disjunctive conditionals, and apply the conditions to evaluate the validity of a hypothetical inference.

Core Idea
In qiyas istithna'i, the conclusion is forced by affirming or negating one part of a conditional—the type of conditional determines the result.

This lesson introduces you to the fourth form of qiyas in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: the exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). Unlike the first three forms that compare cases, this form derives a conclusion from a conditional proposition and an exception. Mastering this tool equips you to handle legal arguments that hinge on conditional statements, such as 'If X, then Y' clauses found in rulings. We will walk through the definition, types, conditions, and a real Hanafi example.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
Identify the two premises: a conditional proposition (qadiyya shartiyya) and an exceptive premise that affirms or negates one part. The conclusion follows necessarily.
The exceptive particle is typically 'lākinna' (but).
2
Differentiate conjunctive vs disjunctive
In a conjunctive conditional (shartiyya muttasila), affirming the antecedent affirms the consequent; negating the consequent negates the antecedent. In a disjunctive conditional (shartiyya munfasila), affirming one part negates the other, and negating one affirms the other.
Memorize the pattern: for conjunctive, 'afirm affirms; negate negates'. For disjunctive, 'afirm negates; negate affirms'.
3
Apply the conditions for validity
Three conditions: (1) The conditional must be affirmative; (2) Conjunctive must be necessary (luzumiyya), disjunctive must be exclusive (anadiyya); (3) Both the conditional and the exception must be universal (kulliyya). If any condition is missing, the inference is invalid.
A negative conditional yields no conclusion. If the relation is not necessary or exclusive, the conclusion does not follow.
4
Test with a Hanafi fiqh example
Take the ruling: 'If the price is unknown, then the sale is fasid (voidable).' This is a conjunctive conditional. Then: 'But the price is unknown.' Therefore: 'The sale is fasid.' Verify conditions: the conditional is affirmative, the relation is necessary (unknown price necessarily leads to fasid), and both premises are universal in scope.
This shows how qiyas istithna'i operates in real fatwa reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف النعوت شرح مسلم الثبوت
۱۵۵
ترجمه : چوتھی صورت یہ ہے کہ دو امر کے درمیان ملازمت ثابت کر دیا جائے تو اس میں وضع مقدم وضع تالی کا نتیجہ دے گا ورنہ دونوں امر کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہے گا اور اس کا عکس نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے کہ ممکن ہے کہ لازم عام ہو اور رفع برعکس وضع ہے، اور اعتراض کیا گیا ہے کہ تالی کارفع مقدم کے رفع کو ستلزم ہونا ممنوع ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ انتفاء لازم محال ہو پس جب انتفاء لازم کا وقوع فرض کر لیا جائے تو لزوم باقی نہیں رہ جائے گا تو ملزوم کا اقتفاء لازم نہیں آئے گا میں کہوں گا کہ لزوم حقیقت میں تمام اوقات و جملہ تقادیر میں انفکاک کے امتناع کا نام ہے لہذا وقت انفکاک اور وہ لزوم کا باقی نہ رہنا ہے، جمیع تقادیر میں داخل ہے غرض یہ اعتراض تو منع لزوم کی طرف راجع ہے حالانکہ لزوم فرض کیا گیا ہے یہ خلاف مفروض ہے اسلئے غور کرو!
تشریح : - قیاس کے صور خمسہ قریبہ میں سے چوتھی صورت قیاس استثنائی کا ذکر اس عبارت میں ہے۔ اور شکل رابع کو مصنف نے ترک کر دیا کہ وہ قریب الانتاج نہیں ہوتا بلکہ بعید از قیاس ہے۔ اس کے بر عکس شکل ثانی و ثالث چونکہ بعید از قیاس نہیں ہیں بلکہ قریب الانتاج ہوتے ہیں اس لئے قریبہ میں داخل میں چونکہ شکل ثانی کو شکل اول کی طرف نقل کرنے کے لئے نقیض نتیجہ کو صغری بنا دینا کافی ہے ایسے ہی شکل ثالث کو اول کی طرف پھیرنے کے لئے نقیض نتیجہ کو کبری بنا دینا کافی ہے کسی مقدمہ اجنبیہ کے سہارا لینے کی ضرورت نہیں پڑتی جیسا کہ گذرا ۔ اس لئے مصنف نے صرف اول و ثانی اور ثالث کو ذکر کیا اور رابع کو ترک کر دیا پھر شروع کیا قیاس استثنائی کے بیان میں تو کہا الرابعة ان يثبت الملازمة الخ ۔ قوله الرابعة ان يثبت الملازمة بين أمرين الخ
اس عبارت سے قیاس استثنائی کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ اس کی تفصیل مندرجہ ذیل ہے۔ قیاس استثنائی :۔ اس کو کہتے ہیں جس میں میں نتیجہ یا نقیض نتیجہ بالعل مذکور ہو۔ یہ قیاس بھی دو مقدمہ سے مرکب ہوتا ہے اولا ایک قضیہ شرطیہ کو ذکر کرتے ہیں پھر حرف استثنائی لکن“ کے ذریعہ دوسرا مقدمہ وضعیہ لاتے ہیں جس میں اس کے دونوں جزؤوں میں سے ایک کا اثبات یا رفع ہوتا ہے تا که جزء آخر کی وضع یا اسکارفع لازم ہو سکے۔ شرطیہ متصلہ میں اس کی مثال اس طرح دی جاتی ہے۔ كلما كانت الشمس طالعة فالنهار موجود ، لكن الشمس طالعة - ج أن النهار موجود لكن النهار ليس بموجود ينتج ، أن الشمس ليست بطالعة اور شرطیہ منفصلہ میں اس کی مثال یہ آتی ہے۔
دائماً اما أن يكون هذا العدد زوجاً او فرداً، لكن هذا العد دزوج ينتج انه ليس بفرد ...... ولكنه ليس بزوج ينتج انه فرد
ان دونوں مثالوں سے ظاہر ہے کہ قیاس کی ترتیب شرطیہ متصلہ کے طور پر ہو تو وضع ( ثبوت و وجود ) وضع کا نتیجہ دے گا اور رفع (نفی) رفع کا نتیجہ دیتا ہے اس کے برعکس قیاس کی ترتیب اگر شرطیہ منفصلہ کے طریق پر ہوئی تو وضع رفع کا اور رفع وضع کا نتیجہ دے گا۔
شرائط : - قیاس استثنائی کے انتاج کی چند شرطیں یہ ہیں ۔
(۱) شرطیہ موجبہ ہو۔ پس اگر شرطیہ سالبہ ہوگا تو وضع ورفع میں سے کچھ بھی نتیجہ نہ دے گا۔ (۲) شرطیہ اگر متصلہ ہو تو اس کے لئے لزومیہ ہونا شرط ہے اور منفصلہ ہو تو عناد یہ ہونا شرط ہے۔ (۳) دوامر میں سے ایک ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ شرطیہ کلیہ ہو دوسرا یہ کہ استثنا ، یعنی وضع ورفع کلیہ ہو۔ حاصل عبارت : ماتن کی عبارت کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ دو امر مثلا طلوع شمس اور وجود نہار کے درمیان ملازمت ثابت ہو بایں طور کہ جب جب ان دونوں امر میں سے ایک ثابت ہوتو دوسرا بھی ثابت ہو جائے جیسے كـلـمـا كـانـت الشمس طالعة فالنهار موجود پھر اب لکن کے ذریعہ اگر مقدم کا ثبوت و وضع مذکور ہو تو نتیجہ تالی کے وضع و ثبوت کا ہوگا جیسے مثال مذکور ہیں لكن الشمس طالعة“ میں ذکر مقدم بطور وضع تحقق کے ہے اس لئے نتیجہ بھی تالی کے وضع وتحقیق کا ہوا جیسے فالنھار موجود اگر وضع مقدم ، وضع تالی کا نتیجہ نہ دے تو مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گا کہ ملزوم کا تحقق لازم کے تحقق کو ستلزم ہے اور اس مقام پر یہی مفروض ہے کہ تالی مقدم کے لئے لازم اور مقدم اسکا ملزوم ہے لہذا مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم کی نفی خلاف مفروض ہے۔ البتہ تالی کا تحقق وضع مقدم کے وضع کا نتیجہ نہ دے گا اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ تالی جو لازم ہے مقدم ملزوم کا، ملزوم سے اہم ہو تو تحقق لازم تحقق ملزم کا نتیجہ نہیں دے سکتا کیونکہ اعم کا حق اخص کے تحق موستلزم نہیں ہوتا جسے تحق حیوان تحقیق انسان کو زم نہیں ۔ ہاں البتہ اگر رفع تالی مقصود ہو تو رفع تالی رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دے گا کہ لازم کا رفع ملزوم کے
Translation: The fourth form is that when a necessary relation is established between two matters, then the affirmation of the antecedent yields the affirmation of the consequent; otherwise, the necessary relation will not remain between the two matters, and its converse is not possible because the necessary concomitant may be more general, and negation is the opposite of affirmation. An objection has been raised that it is not conceded that the negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent, because it is possible that the non-existence of the necessary concomitant is impossible. So when the occurrence of the non-existence of the necessary concomitant is assumed, then the necessary relation will not remain, and the necessitated will not be followed by the necessary concomitant. I say: Necessary relation in reality is the name for the impossibility of separation in all times and all states; therefore the time of separation and the non-remaining of that necessary relation is included in all states. In short, this objection reverts to denying the necessary relation, whereas the necessary relation is assumed, so it is contrary to the assumption. Therefore ponder! Explanation: Among the five near forms of qiyas, the fourth form is the exceptive syllogism, which is mentioned in this passage. And the author has omitted the fourth figure because it is not near to producing a conclusion, but rather far from qiyas. In contrast, the second and third figures, since they are not far from qiyas but rather near to producing a conclusion, are included among the near forms. Since to convert the second figure to the first, it is sufficient to make the contradictory of the conclusion the minor premise; similarly, to convert the third figure to the first, it is sufficient to make the contradictory of the conclusion the major premise; there is no need to resort to any extraneous premise, as has passed. Therefore the author only mentioned the first, second, and third and omitted the fourth. Then he began the discussion of the exceptive syllogism, saying: 'The fourth: that the necessary relation is established,' etc. His statement: 'The fourth: that the necessary relation is established between two matters,' etc. This passage indicates the exceptive syllogism. Its detail is as follows. Exceptive syllogism: It is called that in which the conclusion or the contradictory of the conclusion is explicitly mentioned. This syllogism is also composed of two premises: first, a conditional proposition is mentioned; then, by means of the exceptive particle 'lākinna', a second predicative premise is brought in which affirms or negates one of its two parts, so that the affirmation or negation of the other part becomes necessary. In a conjunctive conditional, its example is given as: 'Whenever the sun is rising, then day exists; but the sun is rising' - therefore day exists. 'But day does not exist' - it yields that the sun is not rising. And in a disjunctive conditional, its example is: 'Always either this number is even or odd; but this number is even' - it yields that it is not odd. 'But it is not even' - it yields that it is odd. From both these examples it is evident that if the syllogism is organized according to the conjunctive conditional, then affirmation yields affirmation, and negation yields negation. On the contrary, if the syllogism is organized according to the disjunctive conditional, then affirmation yields negation, and negation yields affirmation. Conditions: There are several conditions for the production of conclusion in the exceptive syllogism: (1) The conditional must be affirmative; if it is negative, it will not yield any conclusion from affirmation or negation. (2) If the conditional is conjunctive, it must be necessary; if it is disjunctive, it must be exclusive. (3) Two matters are necessary: one, that the conditional be universal; second, that the exception, i.e., the affirmation or negation, be universal. Summary of the statement: The gist of the author's statement is that a necessary relation is established between two matters, e.g., sunrise and the existence of day, in such a way that whenever one of these two matters is established, the other is also established, like 'Whenever the sun is rising, day exists.' Then now, by means of 'lākinna', if the antecedent is mentioned as affirmation and establishment, then the conclusion will be the affirmation and establishment of the consequent, as in the mentioned example 'but the sun is rising' where the antecedent is mentioned as affirmation and realization, so the conclusion is also the affirmation and realization of the consequent, like 'then day exists.' If the affirmation of the antecedent does not yield the affirmation of the consequent, then the necessary relation between antecedent and consequent will not remain, because the realization of the necessitated entails the realization of the necessary concomitant, and in this place it is assumed that the consequent is necessary for the antecedent and the antecedent is its necessitated; therefore denying the necessary relation between antecedent and consequent is contrary to the assumption. However, the realization of the consequent will not yield the realization of the antecedent, because it is possible that the consequent, which is the necessary concomitant of the antecedent, is more general than the antecedent; then the realization of the general does not necessitate the realization of the specific, like the realization of animal does not necessitate the realization of man. Yes, if the negation of the consequent is intended, then the negation of the consequent yields the negation of the antecedent, because the negation of the necessary concomitant necessitates the negation of the necessitated.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is an explanation (sharh) of the fourth form of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, specifically the exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i). The author begins by translating the original matn: the fourth form involves establishing a necessary relation (luzum) between two matters. If the antecedent (muqaddam) is affirmed, the consequent (tali) is affirmed; but the converse is not always true because the consequent may be more general. Then he addresses an objection: if the negation of the consequent is assumed, it might not negate the antecedent if the consequent is impossible. But he argues that luzum means inseparability in all states, so assuming separation contradicts the assumption of luzum. In the Tashrih section, he explains that the author of the matn omitted the fourth figure (shakl rabi) because it is not productive; only the first three figures are discussed. He then defines qiyas istithna'i: it consists of two premises: a conditional proposition (qadiyya shartiyya) and an exceptive premise that affirms or negates one part. In a conjunctive conditional (shartiyya muttasila), affirming the antecedent affirms the consequent; negating the consequent negates the antecedent. In a disjunctive conditional (shartiyya munfasila), affirming one disjunct negates the other, and negating one affirms the other. Examples are given from logic (sun/day and even/odd). Finally, three conditions are listed for validity: (1) the conditional must be affirmative; (2) if conjunctive, it must be necessary (luzumiyya); if disjunctive, exclusive (anadiyya); (3) both the conditional and the exception must be universal. This logical tool is used in Hanafi usul to derive rulings from conditional proofs.

Key Terms
قیاس استثنائی (qiyas istithna'i): A syllogism where the conclusion or its contradictory is explicitly mentioned in one premise, and the other premise is a conditional with an exception.
قضیہ شرطیہ (qadiyya shartiyya): A conditional proposition that states a relationship between two clauses, either conjunctive (متصلة) or disjunctive (منفصلة).
ملازمت (mulazamat): The necessary relation between two matters such that one cannot exist without the other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a valid condition for the exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i)?
A) The conditional must be negative.
B) The conditional must be universal and affirmative.
C) The exception must be particular.
D) The relation in a disjunctive conditional must be necessary.

Key Takeaway
The exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) is a rigorous logical tool for deriving conclusions from conditional legal propositions, provided the conditional is affirmative, the relation is necessary (conjunctive) or exclusive (disjunctive), and both premises are universal.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Rules and Conditions of the Exceptive Syllogism
Explicating logical rules of exceptive syllogism with examples and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of conditionals (conjunctive and disjunctive) in an exceptive syllogism and apply the three conditions for a valid conclusion.

Core Idea
Affirming a conjunctive antecedent affirms the consequent; affirming a disjunctive component negates the other.

The exceptive syllogism (qiyas istithna'i) is a logical form used in Hanafi usul to derive rulings from conditional premises. This lesson explains the two main types of conditional propositions—conjunctive and disjunctive—and the essential conditions for a valid inference.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish conjunctive vs disjunctive conditionals
Identify whether the conditional links two propositions such that one necessarily follows the other (conjunctive) or they are mutually exclusive (disjunctive). The text uses examples: 'If the sun is rising, then day exists' (conjunctive) and 'Either this number is even or odd' (disjunctive).
Conjunctive is also called 'shartiyya muttasila'; disjunctive is 'shartiyya munfasila'.
2
Apply the affirmation/negation patterns
For conjunctive: affirming the antecedent (wad' muqaddam) affirms the consequent; negating the antecedent (raf' muqaddam) negates the consequent. For disjunctive: affirming one component negates the other; negating one affirms the other.
These patterns are derived from the necessary correlation (luzum) in conjunctive and exclusivity (inad) in disjunctive.
3
Check the three conditions
(1) The conditional must be affirmative (positive). (2) If conjunctive, it must be necessary (luzumiyya); if disjunctive, it must be exclusive (inadiyya). (3) Either the conditional itself must be universal (kulliyya) or the exception (istithna') must be universal.
If any condition is missing, the syllogism yields no valid conclusion.

النهار موجود لكن النهار ليس بموجود ينتج ، أن الشمس ليست بطالعة اور شرطیہ منفصلہ میں اس کی مثال یہ آتی ہے۔
دائماً اما أن يكون هذا العدد زوجاً او فرداً، لكن هذا العد دزوج ينتج انه ليس بفرد ...... ولكنه ليس بزوج ينتج انه فرد
ان دونوں مثالوں سے ظاہر ہے کہ قیاس کی ترتیب شرطیہ متصلہ کے طور پر ہو تو وضع ( ثبوت و وجود ) وضع کا نتیجہ دے گا اور رفع (نفی) رفع کا نتیجہ دیتا ہے اس کے برعکس قیاس کی ترتیب اگر شرطیہ منفصلہ کے طریق پر ہوئی تو وضع رفع کا اور رفع وضع کا نتیجہ دے گا۔
شرائط : - قیاس استثنائی کے انتاج کی چند شرطیں یہ ہیں ۔
(۱) شرطیہ موجبہ ہو۔ پس اگر شرطیہ سالبہ ہوگا تو وضع ورفع میں سے کچھ بھی نتیجہ نہ دے گا۔ (۲) شرطیہ اگر متصلہ ہو تو اس کے لئے لزومیہ ہونا شرط ہے اور منفصلہ ہو تو عناد یہ ہونا شرط ہے۔ (۳) دوامر میں سے ایک ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ شرطیہ کلیہ ہو دوسرا یہ کہ استثنا ، یعنی وضع ورفع کلیہ ہو۔ حاصل عبارت : ماتن کی عبارت کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ دو امر مثلا طلوع شمس اور وجود نہار کے درمیان ملازمت ثابت ہو بایں طور کہ جب جب ان دونوں امر میں سے ایک ثابت ہوتو دوسرا بھی ثابت ہو جائے جیسے كـلـمـا كـانـت الشمس طالعة فالنهار موجود پھر اب لکن کے ذریعہ اگر مقدم کا ثبوت و وضع مذکور ہو تو نتیجہ تالی کے وضع و ثبوت کا ہوگا جیسے مثال مذکور ہیں لكن الشمس طالعة“ میں ذکر مقدم بطور وضع تحقق کے ہے اس لئے نتیجہ بھی تالی کے وضع وتحقیق کا ہوا جیسے فالنھار موجود اگر وضع مقدم ، وضع تالی کا نتیجہ نہ دے تو مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گا کہ ملزوم کا تحقق لازم کے تحقق کو ستلزم ہے اور اس مقام پر یہی مفروض ہے کہ تالی مقدم کے لئے لازم اور مقدم اسکا ملزوم ہے لہذا مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم کی نفی خلاف مفروض ہے۔ البتہ تالی کا تحقق وضع مقدم کے وضع کا نتیجہ نہ دے گا اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ تالی جو لازم ہے مقدم ملزوم کا، ملزوم سے اہم ہو تو تحقق لازم تحقق ملزم کا نتیجہ نہیں دے سکتا کیونکہ اعم کا حق اخص کے تحق موستلزم نہیں ہوتا جسے تحق حیوان تحقیق انسان کو زم نہیں ۔ ہاں البتہ اگر رفع تالی مقصود ہو تو رفع تالی رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دے گا کہ لازم کا رفع ملزوم کے رفع کو یا اعم کا انتفاء اخص کے انتظاء وستلزم ہوتا ہے مگر مقدم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کا نتیجہ نہیں دیتا اس لئے کہ ملزوم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کو ستلزم نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ ملزوم اخص ہو اور لازم اہم ہو اور یہ مسلم کہ اخص کے رفع سے عام کا رفع لازم نہیں آتا چنانچہ انسان کے انتفاء سے حیوان کا انتفاء اور آگ کے انتفاء سے حرارت کا انتفاءلازم نہیں ۔
قوله واورد منع استلزام الرفع الرفع لجواز استحالة الخ ماتن کے قول و الرفع بالعکس پر ایک اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے درج بالا عبارت میں اسی اعتراض کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔
اعتراض: کی تقریر یہ ہے معترض کہتا ہے کہ ہمکو تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع ہوستلزم ہے اسلئے کہ ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ کوئی ایک ایسا قضیہ شرطیہ ہو جس میں تالی یعنی لازم کا انتفاء مقدم یعنی ملزوم سے محال ہو مطلب یہ ہے کہ شرطیہ میں ایسی تالی ولازم ہو کہ اپنے مقدم و ملزوم کے ساتھ ہمیشہ قائم ہو اس کا انفکاک اس سے محال ہو پس جب اس تالی کو جس کا انتفاء اور انفکاک محال ہے کا اگر وقوع فرض کر لیا جائے تو دوسرا استحالہ یہ لازم آئے گا کہ قضیہ شرطیہ کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گالہذا ایک محال محال آخر کو ستلزم ہوگا ۔ جب ایک محال (انتفاء لازم) کا وقوع فرض کر لینے سے دوسرا محال ( عدم بقا ۔ لزوم ) لازم آیا تو شرطیہ میں لزوم باقی نہ رہا لہذا انتفاء لازم سے انتفاء ملزوم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس تقدیر پر تالی لازم نہ رہی اور ملز وم ملزوم ہی نہ رہا کہ اس کا انتفاء لازم آئے الغرض انتفاء تالی انتظاء مقدم موستلزم نہیں ہے۔
قوله اقول اللزوم حقيقة امتناع الانفكاك ...... قد فرض جواب اس عبارت سے اعتراض مذکور کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو اس وقت مستلزم ہے جب مقدم و نالی کے درمیان رشتہ بلزوم بر قرار رہے اور آپ نے جو صورت پیش کی ہے کہ انتفاء تالی بغیر انتفاء مقدم کے پایا گیا ہے تو اس لئے کہ اس میں نسبت لزوم ہی نہ رہی غرض رفع تالی ، رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دینے کی جو بنیاد تھی کہ مقدم و تالی کے درمیان لزوم باقی رہے وہی منفی ہے۔ لہذا یہ اعتراض ہمکو مصر نہیں کیونکہ قضیہ شرطیہ کلیہ میں جو لزوم معتبر ہے اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مقدم سے تالی کا انفکاک جمیع اوقات و تقادیر میں ممتنع ہو حالانکہ
The day exists but the day does not exist produces that the sun is not rising. And in the disjunctive conditional, its example comes: Always, either this number is even or odd, but this number is even produces that it is not odd... and it is not even produces that it is odd. From both these examples it is clear that when the syllogism is arranged in the form of a conjunctive conditional, then affirmation (wad') yields affirmation and negation (raf') yields negation. Conversely, if the syllogism is arranged in the way of a disjunctive conditional, then affirmation yields negation and negation yields affirmation.
Conditions: For the production of a conclusion in an exceptive syllogism, there are several conditions: (1) The conditional must be affirmative, because if the conditional is negative, it will not yield any conclusion from affirmation or negation. (2) If the conditional is conjunctive, it must be necessary (luzumiyya); if it is disjunctive, it must be exclusive (inadiyya). (3) One of two things is necessary: either the conditional must be universal, or the exception (istithna') i.e. the affirmation or negation must be universal. Summary of the expression: The summary of the author's expression is that a correlation is established between two matters, e.g., sunrise and existence of daytime, in such a way that whenever one of these two matters is established, the other is also established, like 'Whenever the sun is rising, the day exists.' Then, through 'lakinna' if the affirmation or establishment of the antecedent is mentioned, the result will be the affirmation and establishment of the consequent, as in the mentioned example: 'But the sun is rising' – here the antecedent is mentioned by way of affirmation and verification, so the result is also the affirmation and verification of the consequent, like 'So the day exists.' If the affirmation of the antecedent does not result in the affirmation of the consequent, then the correlation between antecedent and consequent would not remain, because the verification of the correlative necessitates the verification of the necessary. And at this place it is presumed that the consequent is necessary for the antecedent and the antecedent is its correlative; therefore negating the correlation between antecedent and consequent contradicts the presumption. However, the verification of the consequent does not result from the affirmation of the antecedent, because it is possible that the consequent – which is necessary for the antecedent correlative – is more general than the correlative, so the verification of the necessary cannot result in the verification of the correlative, because the more general does not necessitate the more particular; e.g., the verification of animal does not necessitate the verification of human. Yes, however, if the negation of the consequent is intended, then the negation of the consequent yields the negation of the antecedent, because the negation of the necessary necessitates the negation of the correlative, or the non-existence of the more general necessitates the non-existence of the more particular. But the negation of the antecedent does not yield the negation of the necessary, because the negation of the correlative does not necessitate the negation of the necessary, since it is possible that the correlative is more particular and the necessary is more general, and it is accepted that the negation of the particular does not necessitate the negation of the general. Thus, the non-existence of human does not necessitate the non-existence of animal, and the non-existence of fire does not necessitate the non-existence of heat.
His statement: 'And he raised an objection: denial of the entailment of negation for negation due to the possibility of impossibility...' On the author's statement 'and negation conversely', an objection occurs. In the above passage, there is an indication to this objection.
The objection: Its formulation is that the objector says: We do not accept that the negation of the consequent entails the negation of the antecedent, because it is possible that there is a conditional proposition in which the consequent (i.e., the necessary) is impossible to be absent from the antecedent (i.e., the correlative). The meaning is that in the conditional, there is such a consequent and necessary that it is always established with its antecedent and correlative; its separation from it is impossible. So when this consequent, whose non-existence and separation is impossible, is assumed to occur, then another impossibility follows: that the correlation within the conditional proposition would not remain. Therefore, one impossibility entails another impossibility. When from assuming the occurrence of one impossibility (the non-existence of the necessary) another impossibility (the non-remaining of correlation) follows, then correlation does not remain in the conditional. Hence, the non-existence of the necessary does not result in the non-existence of the correlative, because on this assumption the consequent is no longer necessary and the correlative is not a correlative such that its non-existence would be entailed. In short, the non-existence of the consequent does not entail the non-existence of the antecedent.
His statement: 'I say: correlation in reality is the impossibility of separation... it is assumed.' The answer: This passage indicates the response to the aforementioned objection. The summary of the response is that our claim is that the negation of the consequent entails the negation of the antecedent only when the relationship of correlation between antecedent and consequent remains established. And you have presented a case where the non-existence of the consequent is found without the non-existence of the antecedent – this is because in that case the relation of correlation did not remain. In short, the basis for the negation of the consequent yielding the negation of the antecedent – that correlation remains between antecedent and consequent – is negated. Therefore, this objection does not apply to us, because by the correlation that is considered in a universal conditional proposition, it is meant that the separation of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible in all times and circumstances; whereas
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut, explains the logical rules governing the exceptive syllogism (قیاس استثنائی) which is crucial for deriving fiqh rulings through analogy. The commentator begins with a clear distinction between conjunctive and disjunctive conditionals using examples from natural phenomena (sun/day) and mathematics (even/odd). He establishes that in a conjunctive conditional, affirming the antecedent affirms the consequent, and negating it negates the consequent; in a disjunctive conditional, affirming one component negates the other, and negating one affirms the other. This logic mirrors Hanafi usul's method of reasoning with conditional premises.

The author then enumerates three conditions for a valid exceptive syllogism: (1) the conditional must be affirmative; (2) it must be either necessary (لزومیہ) for conjunctive or exclusive (عنادیہ) for disjunctive; (3) either the conditional or the exception must be universal. He elaborates on the nature of necessary correlation (لزوم) using the example of sunrise and daytime. A key nuance is that the more general (اعم) does not necessitate the more specific (اخص), so affirming a broader consequent does not affirm the narrower antecedent, but negating the broader consequent does negate the broader antecedent due to the correlation.

The commentator addresses an objection: if the consequent is necessarily always present, its non-existence is impossible, so assuming its non-existence would break the correlation, thus the entailment of negation for negation fails. The response clarifies that the entailment holds only when the correlation remains intact by definition. In a universal conditional, the impossibility of separation is assumed, so the objection mistakenly assumes a scenario that contradicts the very condition of correlation. Thus, the Hanafi logical framework is defended.

Key Terms
شرطیہ متصلہ (shartiyya muttasila): Conjunctive conditional where the antecedent necessarily implies the consequent in all cases.
شرطیہ منفصلہ (shartiyya munfasila): Disjunctive conditional where the parts are mutually exclusive; affirming one negates the other and vice versa.
قیاس استثنائی (qiyas istithna'i): A syllogism that draws a conclusion by excepting (affirming or negating) one part of a conditional.
لزوم (luzum): Necessary correlation between antecedent and consequent such that separation is impossible in all circumstances.
وضع (wad'): Affirmation or establishment of a proposition in a conditional context.
رفع (raf'): Negation or removal of a proposition in a conditional context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a conjunctive conditional that is affirmative and necessary, if the antecedent is affirmed (وضع مقدم), what is the logical result regarding the consequent?
A) The consequent is negated.
B) The consequent is affirmed.
C) No conclusion can be drawn.
D) The entire conditional becomes false.

Key Takeaway
The exceptive syllogism yields a valid conclusion only when the conditional is affirmative, necessary (or exclusive), and universal.

The Asymmetry of Affirmation and Negation and Defense of Negation Entailment
Defense of the negation entailment against an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why negation of the consequent entails negation of the antecedent only when the correlation remains, and evaluate the objection that denying entailment due to impossibility.

Core Idea
Negation of the wider (consequent/general) entails negation of the narrower (antecedent/particular), but not vice versa.

Building on the rules of exceptive syllogism, this lesson delves into the asymmetry between affirmation and negation. It addresses a critical objection about the entailment of negation and defends the Hanafi position by clarifying the role of necessary correlation.

Guided Path
1
State the one-way entailment rule
Negation of consequent (raf' tali) entails negation of antecedent (raf' muqaddam) only if the correlation (luzum) remains. The text shows this via the general-particular relationship: non-existence of the general entails non-existence of the particular that falls under it.
This is derived from the principle: 'رفع لازم رفع ملزوم' (negation of the necessary negates the correlative).
2
Understand the general-particular relationship
The more general (a'amm) does not necessitate the more particular (akhass) when affirming, but negation of the general does necessitate negation of the particular. Example: non-existence of animal entails non-existence of human, but existence of animal does not entail existence of human.
This is illustrated in the text with 'animal/human' and 'fire/heat' examples.
3
Analyze the objection
The objector says: If the consequent is necessarily always present (inseparable from antecedent), then assuming its non-existence is an impossibility. This would break the correlation, so the entailment fails. The objection is presented in the text as 'واورد منع استلزام الرفع الرفع لجواز استحالة'.
The objector is not named; this is a hypothetical logical objection.
4
Apply the Hanafi response
The response clarifies that the entailment holds only when the correlation is maintained. In the objector's scenario, the correlation is broken by assuming the impossible; thus the scenario does not refute the rule. The text says: 'قول اقول اللزوم حقيقة امتناع الانفكاك...' meaning correlation is defined as impossibility of separation, and the assumption of non-existence contradicts that.
The response effectively shows that the objector misapplies the condition of the syllogism.

النهار موجود لكن النهار ليس بموجود ينتج ، أن الشمس ليست بطالعة اور شرطیہ منفصلہ میں اس کی مثال یہ آتی ہے۔
دائماً اما أن يكون هذا العدد زوجاً او فرداً، لكن هذا العد دزوج ينتج انه ليس بفرد ...... ولكنه ليس بزوج ينتج انه فرد

(۱) شرطیہ موجبہ ہو۔ پس اگر شرطیہ سالبہ ہوگا تو وضع ورفع میں سے کچھ بھی نتیجہ نہ دے گا۔ (۲) شرطیہ اگر متصلہ ہو تو اس کے لئے لزومیہ ہونا شرط ہے اور منفصلہ ہو تو عناد یہ ہونا شرط ہے۔ (۳) دوامر میں سے ایک ہونا ضروری ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ شرطیہ کلیہ ہو دوسرا یہ کہ استثنا ، یعنی وضع ورفع کلیہ ہو۔ حاصل عبارت : ماتن کی عبارت کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ دو امر مثلا طلوع شمس اور وجود نہار کے درمیان ملازمت ثابت ہو بایں طور کہ جب جب ان دونوں امر میں سے ایک ثابت ہوتو دوسرا بھی ثابت ہو جائے جیسے كـلـمـا كـانـت الشمس طالعة فالنهار موجود پھر اب لکن کے ذریعہ اگر مقدم کا ثبوت و وضع مذکور ہو تو نتیجہ تالی کے وضع و ثبوت کا ہوگا جیسے مثال مذکور ہیں لكن الشمس طالعة“ میں ذکر مقدم بطور وضع تحقق کے ہے اس لئے نتیجہ بھی تالی کے وضع وتحقیق کا ہوا جیسے فالنھار موجود اگر وضع مقدم ، وضع تالی کا نتیجہ نہ دے تو مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گا کہ ملزوم کا تحقق لازم کے تحقق کو ستلزم ہے اور اس مقام پر یہی مفروض ہے کہ تالی مقدم کے لئے لازم اور مقدم اسکا ملزوم ہے لہذا مقدم وتالی کے درمیان لزوم کی نفی خلاف مفروض ہے۔ البتہ تالی کا تحقق وضع مقدم کے وضع کا نتیجہ نہ دے گا اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ تالی جو لازم ہے مقدم ملزوم کا، ملزوم سے اہم ہو تو تحقق لازم تحقق ملزم کا نتیجہ نہیں دے سکتا کیونکہ اعم کا حق اخص کے تحق موستلزم نہیں ہوتا جسے تحق حیوان تحقیق انسان کو زم نہیں ۔ ہاں البتہ اگر رفع تالی مقصود ہو تو رفع تالی رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دے گا کہ لازم کا رفع ملزوم کے رفع کو یا اعم کا انتفاء اخص کے انتظاء وستلزم ہوتا ہے مگر مقدم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کا نتیجہ نہیں دیتا اس لئے کہ ملزوم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کو ستلزم نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ ملزوم اخص ہو اور لازم اہم ہو اور یہ مسلم کہ اخص کے رفع سے عام کا رفع لازم نہیں آتا چنانچہ انسان کے انتفاء سے حیوان کا انتفاء اور آگ کے انتفاء سے حرارت کا انتفاءلازم نہیں ۔
قوله واورد منع استلزام الرفع الرفع لجواز استحالة الخ ماتن کے قول و الرفع بالعکس پر ایک اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے درج بالا عبارت میں اسی اعتراض کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔
اعتراض: کی تقریر یہ ہے معترض کہتا ہے کہ ہمکو تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع ہوستلزم ہے اسلئے کہ ایسا ہوسکتا ہے کہ کوئی ایک ایسا قضیہ شرطیہ ہو جس میں تالی یعنی لازم کا انتفاء مقدم یعنی ملزوم سے محال ہو مطلب یہ ہے کہ شرطیہ میں ایسی تالی ولازم ہو کہ اپنے مقدم و ملزوم کے ساتھ ہمیشہ قائم ہو اس کا انفکاک اس سے محال ہو پس جب اس تالی کو جس کا انتفاء اور انفکاک محال ہے کا اگر وقوع فرض کر لیا جائے تو دوسرا استحالہ یہ لازم آئے گا کہ قضیہ شرطیہ کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گالہذا ایک محال محال آخر کو ستلزم ہوگا ۔ جب ایک محال (انتفاء لازم) کا وقوع فرض کر لینے سے دوسرا محال ( عدم بقا ۔ لزوم ) لازم آیا تو شرطیہ میں لزوم باقی نہ رہا لہذا انتفاء لازم سے انتفاء ملزوم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس تقدیر پر تالی لازم نہ رہی اور ملز وم ملزوم ہی نہ رہا کہ اس کا انتفاء لازم آئے الغرض انتفاء تالی انتظاء مقدم موستلزم نہیں ہے۔
قوله اقول اللزوم حقيقة امتناع الانفكاك ...... قد فرض جواب اس عبارت سے اعتراض مذکور کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو اس وقت مستلزم ہے جب مقدم و نالی کے درمیان رشتہ بلزوم بر قرار رہے اور آپ نے جو صورت پیش کی ہے کہ انتفاء تالی بغیر انتفاء مقدم کے پایا گیا ہے تو اس لئے کہ اس میں نسبت لزوم ہی نہ رہی غرض رفع تالی ، رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دینے کی جو بنیاد تھی کہ مقدم و تالی کے درمیان لزوم باقی رہے وہی منفی ہے۔ لہذا یہ اعتراض ہمکو مصر نہیں کیونکہ قضیہ شرطیہ کلیہ میں جو لزوم معتبر ہے اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مقدم سے تالی کا انفکاک جمیع اوقات و تقادیر میں ممتنع ہو حالانکہ
The day exists but the day does not exist produces that the sun is not rising. And in the disjunctive conditional, its example comes: Always, either this number is even or odd, but this number is even produces that it is not odd... and it is not even produces that it is odd. From both these examples it is clear that when the syllogism is arranged in the form of a conjunctive conditional, then affirmation (wad') yields affirmation and negation (raf') yields negation. Conversely, if the syllogism is arranged in the way of a disjunctive conditional, then affirmation yields negation and negation yields affirmation.
Conditions: For the production of a conclusion in an exceptive syllogism, there are several conditions: (1) The conditional must be affirmative, because if the conditional is negative, it will not yield any conclusion from affirmation or negation. (2) If the conditional is conjunctive, it must be necessary (luzumiyya); if it is disjunctive, it must be exclusive (inadiyya). (3) One of two things is necessary: either the conditional must be universal, or the exception (istithna') i.e. the affirmation or negation must be universal. Summary of the expression: The summary of the author's expression is that a correlation is established between two matters, e.g., sunrise and existence of daytime, in such a way that whenever one of these two matters is established, the other is also established, like 'Whenever the sun is rising, the day exists.' Then, through 'lakinna' if the affirmation or establishment of the antecedent is mentioned, the result will be the affirmation and establishment of the consequent, as in the mentioned example: 'But the sun is rising' – here the antecedent is mentioned by way of affirmation and verification, so the result is also the affirmation and verification of the consequent, like 'So the day exists.' If the affirmation of the antecedent does not result in the affirmation of the consequent, then the correlation between antecedent and consequent would not remain, because the verification of the correlative necessitates the verification of the necessary. And at this place it is presumed that the consequent is necessary for the antecedent and the antecedent is its correlative; therefore negating the correlation between antecedent and consequent contradicts the presumption. However, the verification of the consequent does not result from the affirmation of the antecedent, because it is possible that the consequent – which is necessary for the antecedent correlative – is more general than the correlative, so the verification of the necessary cannot result in the verification of the correlative, because the more general does not necessitate the more particular; e.g., the verification of animal does not necessitate the verification of human. Yes, however, if the negation of the consequent is intended, then the negation of the consequent yields the negation of the antecedent, because the negation of the necessary necessitates the negation of the correlative, or the non-existence of the more general necessitates the non-existence of the more particular. But the negation of the antecedent does not yield the negation of the necessary, because the negation of the correlative does not necessitate the negation of the necessary, since it is possible that the correlative is more particular and the necessary is more general, and it is accepted that the negation of the particular does not necessitate the negation of the general. Thus, the non-existence of human does not necessitate the non-existence of animal, and the non-existence of fire does not necessitate the non-existence of heat.
His statement: 'And he raised an objection: denial of the entailment of negation for negation due to the possibility of impossibility...' On the author's statement 'and negation conversely', an objection occurs. In the above passage, there is an indication to this objection.
The objection: Its formulation is that the objector says: We do not accept that the negation of the consequent entails the negation of the antecedent, because it is possible that there is a conditional proposition in which the consequent (i.e., the necessary) is impossible to be absent from the antecedent (i.e., the correlative). The meaning is that in the conditional, there is such a consequent and necessary that it is always established with its antecedent and correlative; its separation from it is impossible. So when this consequent, whose non-existence and separation is impossible, is assumed to occur, then another impossibility follows: that the correlation within the conditional proposition would not remain. Therefore, one impossibility entails another impossibility. When from assuming the occurrence of one impossibility (the non-existence of the necessary) another impossibility (the non-remaining of correlation) follows, then correlation does not remain in the conditional. Hence, the non-existence of the necessary does not result in the non-existence of the correlative, because on this assumption the consequent is no longer necessary and the correlative is not a correlative such that its non-existence would be entailed. In short, the non-existence of the consequent does not entail the non-existence of the antecedent.
His statement: 'I say: correlation in reality is the impossibility of separation... it is assumed.' The answer: This passage indicates the response to the aforementioned objection. The summary of the response is that our claim is that the negation of the consequent entails the negation of the antecedent only when the relationship of correlation between antecedent and consequent remains established. And you have presented a case where the non-existence of the consequent is found without the non-existence of the antecedent – this is because in that case the relation of correlation did not remain. In short, the basis for the negation of the consequent yielding the negation of the antecedent – that correlation remains between antecedent and consequent – is negated. Therefore, this objection does not apply to us, because by the correlation that is considered in a universal conditional proposition, it is meant that the separation of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible in all times and circumstances; whereas
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Nu'ut, a commentary on Muslim al-Thubut, explains the logical rules governing the exceptive syllogism (قیاس استثنائی) which is crucial for deriving fiqh rulings through analogy. The commentator begins with a clear distinction between conjunctive and disjunctive conditionals using examples from natural phenomena (sun/day) and mathematics (even/odd). He establishes that in a conjunctive conditional, affirming the antecedent affirms the consequent, and negating it negates the consequent; in a disjunctive conditional, affirming one component negates the other, and negating one affirms the other. This logic mirrors Hanafi usul's method of reasoning with conditional premises.

The author then enumerates three conditions for a valid exceptive syllogism: (1) the conditional must be affirmative; (2) it must be either necessary (لزومیہ) for conjunctive or exclusive (عنادیہ) for disjunctive; (3) either the conditional or the exception must be universal. He elaborates on the nature of necessary correlation (لزوم) using the example of sunrise and daytime. A key nuance is that the more general (اعم) does not necessitate the more specific (اخص), so affirming a broader consequent does not affirm the narrower antecedent, but negating the broader consequent does negate the broader antecedent due to the correlation.

The commentator addresses an objection: if the consequent is necessarily always present, its non-existence is impossible, so assuming its non-existence would break the correlation, thus the entailment of negation for negation fails. The response clarifies that the entailment holds only when the correlation remains intact by definition. In a universal conditional, the impossibility of separation is assumed, so the objection mistakenly assumes a scenario that contradicts the very condition of correlation. Thus, the Hanafi logical framework is defended.

Key Terms
شرطیہ متصلہ (shartiyya muttasila): Conjunctive conditional where the antecedent necessarily implies the consequent in all cases.
لزوم (luzum): Necessary correlation between antecedent and consequent such that separation is impossible in all circumstances.
رفع (raf'): Negation or removal of a proposition in a conditional context.
اعم (a'amm): More general; the broader concept that encompasses a more specific one.
اخص (akhass): More specific; the narrower concept subsumed under a general one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi response to the objection, what is the key condition for the entailment 'negation of consequent entails negation of antecedent'?
A) The conditional must be disjunctive.
B) The correlation (luzum) must remain intact between antecedent and consequent.
C) The antecedent must be more general than the consequent.
D) The conditional must be negative.

Key Takeaway
Negation of the consequent entails negation of the antecedent only when the necessary correlation is preserved; the objector's scenario of impossible negation breaks the correlation and thus does not refute the rule.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
15 min
The Principle of Negation of Consequent and Its Condition
Defending the entailment rule against an objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule 'رفع تالی مستلزم رفع مقدم' by correctly identifying when the negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent, and evaluate the logical condition of entailment (luzum).

Core Idea
Negation of the consequent entails negation of the antecedent only if entailment remains in all possible circumstances.

This lesson examines a foundational logical rule in Hanafi usul: if A entails B, then not-B entails not-A. The text presents an objection challenging its universal applicability and a defense based on the nature of 'luzum' (entailment). Understanding this rule is crucial for constructing and critiquing qiyas arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule
State the rule 'رفع تالی مستلزم رفع مقدم' in Arabic and English: 'The negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent.' Recognize that this is a conditional rule that depends on a relationship of necessary entailment (luzum).
The rule is also known as modus tollens in logic.
2
Recognize the objection
The text presents an objection: if the consequent is impossible to negate (i.e., always present with the antecedent), then assuming its negation leads to a breakdown of the conditional itself. Therefore, the rule does not apply in such cases. Paraphrase this objection in your own words.
The objector focuses on a hypothetical scenario where the consequent is inseparable, making its negation impossible.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response argues that the rule holds only when entailment (luzum) remains between antecedent and consequent. In the objector's scenario, by assuming the negation of the consequent, one has already denied the entailment. Thus, the rule still applies conditionally.
The response insists that 'luzum' is defined as prevention of separation in all times and circumstances (امتناع الانفكاك في جميع الأوقات والتقادير).
4
Evaluate the critique of the response
The commentator (Mirza Zahid) critiques the response using the phrase 'فتدبر'. He distinguishes between 'all circumstances' and 'all possible circumstances'. The time of separation is not a possible circumstance for the consequent because the consequent cannot exist in that scenario. Thus, the author's response is flawed.
This critique relies on the nuance of 'ممکن' (possible) in the definition of luzum.
5
Apply the refined rule
Apply the refined understanding: the rule 'رفع تالی مستلزم رفع مقدم' holds when the time/place of negation is among the possible circumstances where the antecedent can exist. If not, the rule does not apply. Think of a simple qiyas example where this rule is used.
Example: 'If it rains, the ground is wet. The ground is not wet → it did not rain.' This works because the negation of 'wet ground' is a possible circumstance when rain is absent.

رفع کو یا اعم کا انتفاء اخص کے انتفاء سے لازم ہوتا ہے مگر مقدم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کا نتیجہ نہیں دیتا اس لئے کہ ملزوم کا رفع لازم کے رفع کو مستلزم نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ ملزوم اخص ہو اور لازم اہم ہو اور یہ مسلم کہ اخص کے رفع سے عام کا رفع لازم نہیں آتا چنانچہ انسان کے انتفاء سے حیوان کا انتفاء اور آگ کے انتفاء سے حرارت کا انتفاء لازم نہیں.

اعتراض: کی تقریر یہ ہے معترض کہتا ہے کہ ہم کو تسلیم نہیں ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو مستلزم ہے اس لئے کہ ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ کوئی ایک ایسا قضیہ شرطیہ ہو جس میں تالی یعنی لازم کا انتفاء مقدم یعنی ملزوم سے محال ہو مطلب یہ ہے کہ شرطیہ میں ایسی تالی و لازم ہو کہ اپنے مقدم و ملزوم کے ساتھ ہمیشہ قائم ہو اس کا انفکاک اس سے محال ہو پس جب اس تالی کو جس کا انتفاء اور انفکاک محال ہے کا اگر وقوع فرض کر لیا جائے تو دوسرا استحالہ یہ لازم آئے گا کہ قضیہ شرطیہ کے درمیان لزوم نہیں رہ جائے گا لہذا ایک محال محال آخر کو مستلزم ہوگا ۔ جب ایک محال (انتفاء لازم) کا وقوع فرض کر لینے سے دوسرا محال (عدم بقا لزوم) لازم آیا تو شرطیہ میں لزوم باقی نہ رہا لہذا انتفاء لازم سے انتفاء ملزوم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس تقدیر پر تالی لازم نہ رہی اور ملزوم ملزوم ہی نہ رہا کہ اس کا انتفاء لازم آئے الغرض انتفاء تالی انتفاء مقدم کو مستلزم نہیں ہے۔
قوله اقول اللزوم حقيقة امتناع الانفكاك ...... قد فرض جواب اس عبارت سے اعتراض مذکور کے جواب کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ جواب کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ ہمارا دعویٰ یہ ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو اس وقت مستلزم ہے جب مقدم و تالی کے درمیان رشتہ بلزوم برقرار رہے اور آپ نے جو صورت پیش کی ہے کہ انتفاء تالی بغیر انتفاء مقدم کے پایا گیا ہے تو اس لئے کہ اس میں نسبت لزوم ہی نہ رہی غرض رفع تالی، رفع مقدم کا نتیجہ دینے کی جو بنیاد تھی کہ مقدم و تالی کے درمیان لزوم باقی رہے وہی منفی ہے۔ لہذا یہ اعتراض ہم کو مصر نہیں کیونکہ قضیہ شرطیہ کلیہ میں جو لزوم معتبر ہے اس سے مراد یہ ہے کہ مقدم سے تالی کا انفکاک جمیع اوقات و تقادیر میں ممتنع ہو حالانکہ آپنے لزومیہ سے جس وقت لزوم کا انفکاک کیا وہ وقت بھی مقدم و تالی کے درمیان لزوم کے جمیع اوقات میں سے ایک وقت ہے غرض وقت انفکاک بھی مقدم و تالی کے درمیان لزوم کے جملہ اوقات و تقادیر میں داخل ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ وقت انفکاک لزوم کے وقتوں میں سے ایک وقت ہے پس جو ان دونوں کے درمیان لزوم کا وقت تھا اس وقت انفکاک لزوم پایا گیا اس لئے یہ اعتراض مقدم و تالی کے درمیان منع لزوم کی طرف پلٹ گیا جبکہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کو اس وقت مستلزم مانا گیا تھا جب دونوں کے درمیان لزوم باقی ہو اور یہ خلاف مفروض ہے۔
قوله - فتدبر اپنے قول فتدبر سے جواب مذکور کے ضعف بلکہ رد کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ تقریر رو: یہ ہے کہ شرطیہ کلیہ میں مقدم و تالی کے درمیان جو لزوم کی شرط ہے اس لزوم سے جمیع اوقات و تقادیر میں لزوم کی شرط ہونا مراد نہیں ہے بلکہ جملہ اوقات ممکنہ و تقادیر ممکنہ میں لزوم شرط ہے یہ معنی یہ ہے کہ ان تمام تقادیر و اوقات میں لزوم شرط ہے جس میں تالی کا مقدم کے ساتھ اجتماع ممکن ہو سکے اور یہ بہت ظاہر ہے کہ وہ تقدیر جو تالی یا لزوم تالی کے منافی ہے وہ ایسی تقدیر ہے جس میں تالی کا مقدم کے ساتھ اجتماع ممکن نہیں ہے لہذا تقدیر انفکاک لازم ان تمام تقادیر ممکنہ میں داخل ہی نہیں جو شرطیہ میں معتبر ہیں پس مصنف کا یہ کہنا کہ یہ اعتراض منع لزوم کی طرف راجع ہے صحیح نہیں۔ جواب رد: مصنف کے جواب پر جور دو اعتراض کیا گیا اس کے کئی جوابات دیئے گئے ہیں۔ (1) جس دو شے کے درمیان لزوم ہو بایں طور کہ لازم ممتنع الانفکاک ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ وہ لزوم، وجود ملزوم کے جمیع اوقات میں پایا جائے گا پس سوال یہ ہے کہ وقت انفکاک اس جمیع میں داخل ہے یا نہیں! برتقدیر ثانی تسلیم ہے کہ تالی کا رفع مقدم کے رفع کا نتیجہ نہ دے گا چونکہ نتیجہ دینے کے لئے شرط ضروری یہ ہے کہ تقدیر رفع تالی وجود مقدم کے جملہ تقادیر میں داخل ہو حالانکہ اس تقدیر پر یہ فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ وقت انفکاک، وجود مقدم کے جمیع اوقات میں داخل نہیں ہے اور برتقدیر اول یعنی وقت انفکاک اگر وجود مقدم کے جمیع اوقات میں داخل ہے تو اس تقدیر پر بھی نہیں خالی ہوگا کہ تالی لازم کا مقدم سے انفکاک ممتنع ہوگا یا نہیں، برشق ثانی مقدم و تالی دونوں کے مابین لزوم متفق نہ ہوگا تو لزومیہ کلیہ جو قیاس استثنائی کا جزء ہے کا کاذب ہونا لازم آئے گا اور شق اول کہ تالی کا مقدم سے انفکاک ممتنع ہوگا تو اس
The negation of a more general does not necessitate the negation of a more specific; but the negation of the antecedent does not necessarily result in the negation of the consequent because the negation of the necessary condition does not necessitate the negation of the necessary. Because it is possible that the necessary condition is more specific and the consequent is more general, and it is established that negation of the specific does not necessitate negation of the general. Thus, from the non-existence of man, the non-existence of animal does not follow; and from the non-existence of fire, the non-existence of heat does not follow.
His statement: 'And an objection is made regarding the denial of entailment of negation of the negation due to the possibility of impossibility…' The author's statement 'and the negation is opposite' is objected to; the above passage indicates that objection.
The objection: Its exposition is that the objector says: We do not accept that the negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent, because it is possible that there is a conditional proposition in which the negation of the consequent (i.e., the necessary) is impossible from the antecedent (i.e., the necessitating). Meaning that in the conditional, there is such a consequent that always subsists with its antecedent, its separation from it is impossible. Then if we assume the occurrence of that consequent whose negation and separation is impossible, another impossibility would follow: that there would no longer be entailment between the conditional parts. Thus one impossibility would necessitate another impossibility. When from assuming the occurrence of one impossibility (negation of consequent) another impossibility (lack of remaining entailment) follows, then in the conditional, entailment does not remain; therefore, the negation of the consequent does not result in the negation of the antecedent, because under this assumption the consequent is no longer necessary and the antecedent is no longer the necessitating that its negation should follow. In short, the negation of the consequent does not necessitate the negation of the antecedent.
His statement: 'I say: Entailment in reality is the prevention of separation...' This phrase indicates the answer to the mentioned objection. The summary of the answer is: Our claim is that the negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent only when the relationship of entailment between antecedent and consequent remains. And the case you presented—where the negation of the consequent occurs without the negation of the antecedent—is because in it the relationship of entailment no longer existed. Thus, the basis for the negation of the consequent resulting in the negation of the antecedent, namely that entailment remains between antecedent and consequent, is negated. Therefore, this objection does not apply to us, because in a universal conditional, the entailment that is considered means that the separation of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible in all times and circumstances. Yet you, in your [example of] entailment, when you separated the entailment, that time is one of the times of entailment between antecedent and consequent. In short, the time of separation is included among all the times and circumstances of entailment between antecedent and consequent. Consequently, the time of separation is one of the times of entailment. So when there was a time of entailment between the two, at that time the separation of entailment occurred. Therefore, this objection turns into a denial of entailment between antecedent and consequent, whereas the negation of the consequent is considered to necessitate the negation of the antecedent only when entailment remains between them, and this contradicts the assumption.
His statement: 'So contemplate' - by his phrase 'so contemplate' he indicates the weakness, indeed rejection, of the said answer. The exposition is: In a universal conditional, the condition of entailment between antecedent and consequent does not mean entailment in all times and circumstances unconditionally, but entailment is conditioned in all possible times and possible circumstances. The meaning is that entailment is conditioned in all those times and circumstances in which the conjunction of the consequent with the antecedent is possible. And it is quite obvious that the circumstance that contradicts the consequent or its entailment is such a circumstance in which the conjunction of the consequent with the antecedent is not possible. Therefore, the circumstance of separation of the consequent is not included among all those possible circumstances that are considered in the conditional. Hence, the author's statement that this objection reverts to denial of entailment is incorrect. Answer rejection: The author's answer is criticized, and several answers have been given to it. (1) When there is entailment between two things in such a way that the consequent is inseparable, then it is clear that that entailment will be found in all times of the existence of the antecedent. So the question is: Is the time of separation included in that 'all' or not? On the second hypothesis, it is conceded that the negation of the consequent will not result in the negation of the antecedent, because for the result the necessary condition is that the circumstance of negation of the consequent be included among all circumstances of the existence of the antecedent, whereas on this hypothesis it is assumed that the time of separation is not included in all times of the existence of the antecedent. On the first hypothesis—that the time of separation is included in all times of the existence of the antecedent—then even on this hypothesis it will not be free from either that the separation of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible or not. On the second branch, there would be no agreed entailment between antecedent and consequent, so the universal conditional that is part of the syllogism would have to be false. On the first branch—that the separation of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible—then...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of a logical-legal rule: 'the negation of the consequent necessitates the negation of the antecedent' (رفع تالی مستلزم رفع مقدم). This rule is essential in usul al-fiqh for establishing proofs via conditional statements. The Sharh first presents an objection: if the consequent is impossible to negate (i.e., always present with the antecedent), then assuming its negation would lead to the breakdown of the conditional, so the rule doesn't hold universally. The response argues that the rule holds only when entailment (luzum) remains; if we assume the negation of the consequent, we are effectively negating the entailment itself, so the rule still applies. The commentator then critiques this response by distinguishing between all circumstances and possible circumstances, concluding that the time of separation is not among possible circumstances for the consequent, thus the rule remains sound. Finally, the text offers further analysis and alternative answers. Throughout, the discussion follows the Hanafi usul tradition's careful treatment of logical entailment and its conditions.

Key Terms
لزوم (luzūm): Entailment: a relationship where the consequent cannot exist without the antecedent, i.e., separation is impossible in all possible times and circumstances.
رفع تالی (raf‘ tālī): Negation of the consequent in a conditional proposition; used in the rule that negating the consequent entails negating the antecedent.
قضیہ شرطیہ (qaḍiyya sharṭiyya): A conditional proposition consisting of an antecedent (مقدم) and consequent (تالی) linked by entailment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul discussion, what condition must hold for the negation of the consequent to necessitate the negation of the antecedent?
A) The antecedent must be more general than the consequent.
B) The consequent must be impossible to negate.
C) Entailment (luzum) must remain between antecedent and consequent in all possible circumstances.
D) The conditional must be a hypothetical syllogism.

Key Takeaway
The rule 'رفع تالی مستلزم رفع مقدم' is valid only when the negation of the consequent is a possible circumstance that does not violate the inseparability condition of entailment (luzum).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Resolving an Objection on Conditional Lizum in Qiyas Reasoning
Resolves an objection about lizum between antecedent and consequent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the logical objection to conditional lizum and explain the Hanafi commentary's resolution by restricting lizum to times of possible conjunction.

Core Idea
In a universal conditional, lizum applies only where antecedent and consequent can coexist; the time of detachment is excluded.

This passage unpacks a subtle objection regarding the necessity (lizum) between the antecedent and consequent in a conditional statement used in qiyas. The objection claims that the time of detachment (infikak) is included among the times of lizum, which would break the conditional's validity. The commentary refutes this by clarifying that lizum in a universal conditional is restricted to possible conjunctions only, and the time of detachment is not such a time. Two responses are given, each reinforcing the logical integrity of the conditional syllogism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
The objection states: if the time of detachment is one of the times of lizum, then at that time lizum is absent, contradicting the conditional's requirement of constant lizum. This would mean that lifting the consequent does not necessarily lift the antecedent.
2
Understand the first response
The commentary argues that lizum is only required in times where antecedent and consequent can possibly coexist. The time of detachment is not such a time, so the objection fails. The deliberation involves whether the time of detachment is included in the times of lizum or not, leading to two branches.
Follow the logical branches carefully.
3
Analyze the second response
The second response shifts focus: the necessity of entailment (placing for placing, lifting for lifting) holds only when both the concomitance (lizum) and the exception (istithna') are true. The impossibility of the consequent's non-existence proves that the exception is false, so the objection is invalid.
4
Synthesize the resolution
Thus, the objection is resolved by clarifying the scope of lizum: it is not absolute over all times, but only over times where conjunction is possible. The conditional remains valid.
This distinction preserves the logical structure of qiyas.

(۲) اس جگہ بعض اکابر نے یہ افادہ کیا ہے کہ وضع وضع کا اور رفع رفع کا نتیجہ دینے کا لزوم اس وقت ہے جب ملازمت اور استثناء دونوں صادق ہوں لہذا انتفاء لازم کے استحالہ کے جواز کا قول کرنا اسبات کی واضح دلیل ہے کہ استثناء صادق نہیں ہے لہذا ما تن کے قول و الرفع بالعکس “ پر اعتراض ہی درست نہیں۔
From your necessity, at the time you separated the necessity, that time is also one of all the times of necessity between the antecedent and consequent. In short, the time of detachment is also included among all the times and estimations of necessity between the antecedent and consequent. The conclusion is that the time of detachment is one of the times of necessity. So when the time of necessity between them existed, at that time the detachment of necessity occurred. Therefore, this objection reverts to preventing necessity between the antecedent and consequent, since the lifting of the consequent was considered to necessitate the lifting of the antecedent only when necessity remains between them, and this is contrary to the assumption.
His statement - 'fata'ammal' - by his statement 'fata'ammal' he pointed to the weakness, rather refutation, of the mentioned response. The exposition is: In the universal conditional, the condition of necessity between the antecedent and consequent is not meant to be the condition of necessity in all times and estimations; rather, the condition of necessity is in all possible times and possible estimations. The meaning is that the condition of necessity applies to all those estimations and times in which the conjunction of the consequent with the antecedent is possible. It is obvious that the estimation which contradicts the consequent or the necessity of the consequent is an estimation in which the conjunction of the consequent with the antecedent is not possible. Hence, the estimation of detachment of the necessary is not included among all those possible estimations that are considered in the conditional. Therefore, the author's statement that this objection refers back to preventing necessity is not correct. Response to the refutation: Two objections were made against the author's response, and several answers were given. (1) When there is necessity between two things in such a way that the necessary is inseparable, it is obvious that that necessity will be found in all times of existence of the thing to which it is necessary. Then the question is: Is the time of detachment included in all these times or not? On the second assumption, it is conceded that the lifting of the consequent will not result in the lifting of the antecedent, since for giving the result the necessary condition is that the estimation of lifting the consequent be included among all the estimations of the existence of the antecedent. However, on this assumption it is assumed that the time of detachment is not included among all the times of existence of the antecedent. On the first assumption, that is, if the time of detachment is included among all the times of existence of the antecedent, then on this assumption it will not be free from one of two: either the detachment of the necessary from the antecedent is impossible or not. On the second branch, the antecedent and consequent will not [؟] both agree, then the falsehood of the universal conditional, which is part of the exceptive syllogism, will necessarily follow. On the first branch, that the detachment of the consequent from the antecedent is impossible, then on this assumption, the lifting of the consequent necessarily entails the lifting of the antecedent [؟] the desired is obtained. 
(2) In this place, some great scholars have informed that the necessity of giving the result of placing for placing and lifting for lifting is when both the concomitance and the exception are true. Therefore, the statement of the permissibility of the impossibility of the non-existence of the necessary is a clear proof of the affirmation that the exception is not true. Hence, the objection against the matn's statement 'wa al-raf'u bil-'aks' is not valid.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a dispute in the commentary about a logical principle in conditional syllogisms. The objection is that the time of detachment (infikak) is included among the times of necessity (lizum), so the lifting of the consequent would not entail the lifting of the antecedent if necessity is broken. The commentary refutes this by clarifying that the condition of necessity in a universal conditional applies only to possible times where antecedent and consequent can coexist; the time of detachment is not such a time. Then two responses are given: the first shows that if detachment is impossible, the lifting still entails, and if possible, the conditional becomes false. The second response argues that the objection is invalid because the exception (istithna') would not be true. The Hanafi perspective here is about logical rigor in usul al-fiqh reasoning.

Key Terms
لزوم (lizum): Necessity or constant concomitance between two propositions (antecedent and consequent) in a conditional statement.
انفکاک (infikak): Detachment or separation; the breaking of the necessity between antecedent and consequent.
مقدم (muqaddam): The antecedent proposition in a conditional statement.
تالی (tali): The consequent proposition in a conditional statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the objection that the time of detachment invalidates the conditional incorrect?
A) Because lizum is eternal and cannot be detached.
B) Because the conditional's necessity applies only to times when antecedent and consequent can coexist.
C) Because the matn itself says so.
D) Because the time of detachment is impossible.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the lizum in a universal conditional is qualified to possible conjunctions, preserving the validity of qiyas reasoning against objections based on impossible scenarios.

The Three Types of Disjunctive Conditionals
Defines the three standard types of disjunctive conditionals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish the three types of disjunctive conditionals (man'at al-jam', man'at al-khuluw, haqiqiyyah) and apply each to examples from legal reasoning.

Core Idea
A disjunctive conditional is defined by whether it prevents both truths, both falsehoods, or both.

This lesson introduces the classification of disjunctive conditionals, a foundational tool in Hanafi usul al-fiqh for reasoning about mutually exclusive possibilities. Understanding these types helps in constructing sound legal arguments, especially in qiyas and other forms of inference where choices between rulings or 'illahs are required.

Guided Path
1
Understand the structure of a disjunctive conditional
A disjunctive conditional (shartiyyah munfasilah) is a compound proposition consisting of two parts connected by 'or' (أو). Recognize that it presents a choice between two possibilities.
2
Learn the three truth-value patterns
Each type is defined by truth possibilities: man'at al-jam' allows both false but not both true; man'at al-khuluw allows both true but not both false; haqiqiyyah allows neither both true nor both false.
Memorize the definitions with the examples from the text.
3
Apply each type to a simple fiqh scenario
Use a Hanafi legal example to test your understanding. For instance, 'Either this sale is valid or void' is haqiqiyyah because validity and voidness cannot coexist or both be absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متن المسلم : "الخامسة أن تعلم المنافاة بينهما اما صدقاً فقط او كذبا فقط او فيهما فتلزم النتائج بحسبها فتفكر"
ترجمه : پانچویں صورت یہ ہے کہ دو امر کے مابین منافات معلوم کر لیا جائے خواہ صرف صدق میں خواہ صرف کذب میں یا دونوں میں تو نتائج اسی اعتبار سے لازم ہونگے پس ( نتائج پر غور کرو۔
تشریح ۔ صرف قریبہ میں سے یہ پانچویں اور آخری صورت کا بیان ہے جس میں قیاس استثنائی انفصالی کی صورت پیش کی ہے۔ قوله الخامسة أن تعلم المنافاة بينهما اماصدقا فقط الخ اس عبارت میں مصنف نے شرطیہ منفصلہ کی تینوں مشہور قسموں کی تعریفات کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے پھر ان تینوں کے نتائج کی طرف فکر کی دعوت دی ہے۔
اقسام مشہورہ : - شرطیہ منفصلہ کی تین قسمیں ہیں۔
(۱) مانعة الجمع. (۲) مانعة الخلو (۳) حقيقيه
(۱) مانعتہ الجمع: دو امر کے مابین منافات اگر صرف صدق میں ہو بایں طور کہ دونوں بیک وقت صادق نہیں آسکتے ہوں ہاں البتہ دونوں کا ذب ہو سکتے ہیں تو مانعتہ اجمع ہے جیسے امـا أن يكون هذا الشني انسانا او فرسان
(۲) مانعة الخلو - دوامر کے درمیان منافات اگر صرف کذب میں ہو بایں طور کہ دونوں مقدمے بیک وقت غلط نہیں ہو سکتے ہاں البتہ دونوں بیک وقت صادق آ سکتے ہیں تو یہ مانعتہ الخلو ہے جیسے زید اما فی الماء اولا يغرق
(۳) حقیقیہ ۔ دوامر کے درمیان منافات اگر صدق و کذب دونوں میں ہو بایں طور کہ دونوں بیک وقت نہ ہی صادق آ سکتے ہوں نہ ہی دونوں کا ذب ہی ہو سکتے ہیں تو حقیقیہ ہے۔ اما ان يكون هذا
The matn of al-Muslim: 'The fifth is that you know the opposition between them either in truth only, or falsehood only, or in both; then the results are necessary accordingly, so reflect.'
Translation: The fifth situation is that the opposition between two things is known, whether only in truth, only in falsehood, or in both; then the results will be necessary accordingly. So reflect on the results.
Explanation: Among the proximate [forms], this is the fifth and last situation, in which the form of the disjunctive exceptive syllogism is presented. His statement 'the fifth is that you know the opposition between them either in truth only etc.' In this phrase, the author pointed to the definitions of the three famous types of disjunctive conditionals, then invited reflection on their results.
Famous types: There are three types of disjunctive conditionals.
(1) Mutually exclusive (man'at al-jam'): If opposition is only in truth, such that both cannot be true together, but both can be false. Example: Either this thing is a human or a horse.
(2) Mutually exhaustive (man'at al-khuluw): If opposition is only in falsehood, such that both cannot be false together, but both can be true. Example: Zayd is either in water or not drowning.
(3) True disjunction (haqiqiyyah): If opposition is in both truth and falsehood, such that neither can be true together nor false together. Example: Either this is [incomplete].
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the three types of disjunctive conditionals (shartiyyah munfasilah) used in logical reasoning within usul al-fiqh. The matn states the fifth form of conditional syllogisms. The commentary explains that the author refers to the three well-known divisions. Each type is defined by its pattern of truth and falsehood: man'at al-jam' (mutually exclusive) allows both to be false but not both true; man'at al-khuluw (mutually exhaustive) allows both to be true but not both false; haqiqiyyah (true disjunction) allows neither both true nor both false. Examples are given from everyday language. This classification is foundational for understanding disjunctive syllogisms (qiyas istithna'i infisali) which are used in legal reasoning to determine rulings when options are mutually exclusive, exhaustive, or truly contradictory.

Key Terms
مانعة الجمع (man'at al-jam'): A disjunctive conditional that prevents both propositions from being true together, but allows both to be false.
مانعة الخلو (man'at al-khuluw): A disjunctive conditional that prevents both propositions from being false together, but allows both to be true.
حقیقیہ (haqiqiyyah): A true disjunctive conditional that prevents both truth and falsehood together; exactly one proposition is true.
شرطیہ منفصلہ (shartiyyah munfasilah): A disjunctive conditional statement; a compound proposition consisting of two parts connected by 'or' (أو).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of disjunctive conditional is exemplified by 'Either this thing is a human or a horse'?
A) Man'at al-jam'
B) Man'at al-khuluw
C) Haqiqiyyah
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Disjunctive conditionals are classified by their truth patterns: only exclusive, only exhaustive, or both.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
